# Decision log — running paper trail

> **Purpose.** An append-only, chronological record of every **decision / issue / bug / fix / pivot** so that a future session (after auto-compact or a premature end) can reconstruct *what was decided and why* without re-deriving it from faded context. This file exists because on 2026-05-30 the assistant recommended re-opening an **already-settled** decision (build v0.2 vs. a v0.1.3 patch-sweep) — reasoning from in-context memory instead of the durable record. The user: *"we will not have this problem again that you decide something against an already decision line we are already into."*
>
> **Binding usage (see CLAUDE.md "Decision-log discipline"):**
> 1. **Before re-opening ANY decision** — search this file + [`v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md`](v0.1.1-self-test-findings.md) + tasks.md for it. If it's here marked **SETTLED**, do not re-litigate it; execute it. Surface a change only if you have *new* evidence, and say explicitly "this revisits SETTLED decision D-N because <new evidence>".
> 2. **After making/learning anything durable** — append an entry in the SAME batch as the work. Decisions, issues found, bugs, fixes, design choices, pivots. Newest block at the TOP.
> 3. Entry types: **DECISION** (a choice + why), **PIVOT** (a previously-documented choice changed — preserve the old per decision-trail rule), **ISSUE** (a problem noted, maybe not yet fixed), **BUG**, **FIX**, **NOTE**.
> 4. This is the running paper trail. Stable rules still graduate to CLAUDE.md; task state still lives in tasks.md; per-PR narrative still goes to the build log. This file is the chronological spine that ties them together.

---

## 2026-06-01 — the road to a product: ship-one-wow-at-a-time, video-parity is the done-bar

### Settled decisions (do NOT re-open without new evidence)

- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-187: the Kiro CLI default-agent guard was BOM-fragile — a Windows-editor `settings.json` (UTF-8 BOM) made the guard miss an existing `chat.defaultAgent` and CLOBBER the user's default; found by the cut-gate-kiro live-test, fixed kit-wide.** Third live-found cut-blocker of the gate (after D-185/D-186). The KG7 guarded-default probe seeded `settings.json` via PowerShell `Set-Content -Encoding utf8` — which writes a **UTF-8 BOM** (`EF BB BF`). `readDefaultAgentSetting` did a bare `JSON.parse(readFileSync(...))`; the leading BOM makes `JSON.parse` throw → the `catch` returned `null` → the guard concluded "no default agent set" → it wrote `q_cli_default.json`, **taking over the user's default** instead of the guarded `cmk.json`+skipped-existing path. **Unit-green-but-broken-live** (the live-test class): the existing guard unit test seeded BOM-free JSON, so it passed while the real Windows path failed — a BOM on a Windows config file is common, so this is a realistic clobber of a real user's default (the D-184 class again). **Audit found the kit had NO BOM handling anywhere** — `mutate-agent-config.mjs` (which reads the user's `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` + Claude `settings.json`) had the same bare `JSON.parse`, so a BOM'd config there would falsely read as "corrupt" and trigger the refuse-to-clobber error. **The fix (kit-wide, the user's call — "fix it so it is inline with the rest of our code"):** a new shared `read-json.mjs` — `stripBom()` + `parseJsonFile(path, {fallback})` (BOM-tolerant, never-throws). Routed both config readers through it: `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` (`isOurAgent` + `readDefaultAgentSetting` → `parseJsonFile`) and `mutate-agent-config.mjs` (`stripBom` before its existing parse — preserving its distinct empty-vs-corrupt + refuse-to-clobber contract, only the BOM stripped). Test-first: `cli-read-json.test.js` (8: stripBom edge cases + parseJsonFile BOM/missing/malformed) + a kiro-cli-agent guard test seeding the exact BOM that broke it. Verified LIVE: KG7 with a BOM'd `settings.json` → "you already have a Kiro CLI default agent" + `cmk.json` (no clobber). Full suite 2150/0. _Relates D-184 (the clobber class), D-185/D-186 (the gate's other live-found cut-blockers — all unit-green-but-broken-live), the live-test discipline (the BOM only shows on real Windows input), the shared-module discipline (one BOM-tolerant reader, not N inline strips)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-186: the D-185 doctor fix re-introduced the same bug one level down — HC-1 checked only the IDE-hook surface, so a kiro-cli-only install false-FAILed — caught by the skill-review (B1) before merge.** D-185 made HC-1 check `.kiro/hooks/` instead of `.claude/settings.json` — but Kiro wires capture/inject through TWO independent surfaces: the **IDE hooks** (`.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook`, the GUI user) AND the **CLI agent-config** (`~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/{q_cli_default,cmk}.json` with `agentSpawn`/`stop` hooks, the kiro-cli user). D-185 checked only the IDE half → a **kiro-cli-only user** (memory fires via `~/.aws`, no IDE hooks) got a wrong HC-1 FAIL + a heavy `cmk install --ide kiro` hint for a working install. Worse on a clone: `~/.aws` is machine-local and doesn't travel, so the surfaces can legitimately diverge. **This is literally the same separately-correct-jointly-broken class as the original D-185 bug, recursed** — the first fix swapped one hardcoded surface for another instead of checking the CAPABILITY across all surfaces. **The fix:** HC-1 is a capability check — `hc1KiroHooks` PASSes if the IDE hooks OR a cmk-owned CLI agent is present (new exported `hasOurCliAgent({awsDir})` in `kiro-cli-agent.mjs`, keyed on the `managedBy` marker; `awsDir` injectable for tests), FAILs only when NEITHER, and the FAIL names both surfaces. Also tightened `detectInstallKind` to key on the cmk-owned `.kiro/steering/cmk.md` marker (not a bare `.kiro/` dir — I2: a stray `.kiro/` no longer flips the project to the Kiro path) and documented the both-agents precedence punt (I1). Test-first (6 Kiro cases incl. the kiro-cli-only PASS, the I2 stray-dir, neither-FAIL), verified LIVE on the real machine: full install → "wired via IDE hooks + CLI agent"; IDE-hooks-removed copy → "wired via CLI agent" (the false-FAIL is now a correct PASS). **The two-pass review caught this** — self-review missed it; the `code-review-excellence` skill-review's B1 finding is what surfaced it before merge (the discipline working exactly as intended). _Relates D-185 (the fix this corrects — same class recursed), D-184 (the original separately-correct-jointly-broken instance), the two-pass review rule (skill-review caught what self-review missed — the empirical case for it), the cross-agent surfaces (D-182/D-183/D-184)._
- **🐛 BUG + 🔧 FIX (2026-06-21) — D-185: `cmk doctor` was Claude-Code-only; HC-1 false-FAILed on every `--ide kiro` install — found by the v0.4.0 Kiro live-test gate, fixed as a cut-blocker.** Running `cmk doctor` on a real `cmk install --ide kiro` project reported `[FAIL] HC-1: .claude/settings.json missing — hooks not wired → cmk repair --hooks`. **The bug:** HC-1 hard-checked `.claude/settings.json` (Claude Code's hook file) unconditionally — but a Kiro install wires `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook`, and there IS no `.claude/settings.json`. So HC-1 false-FAILed on EVERY Kiro install with a repair hint (`cmk repair --hooks`) for the wrong agent — a scary red FAIL on the headline feature of the release. **Same class as D-184** (the `~/.aws` write bug): the Kiro *installer* was unit-tested in isolation and correct, but the *diagnostic* layer was written before cross-agent install existed and nobody taught it which agent a project was installed for — separately-correct, jointly-broken; only `cmk doctor` on a REAL Kiro install surfaced it (unit tests structurally couldn't — they only ever fed `.claude/settings.json` shapes). **The fix:** `detectInstallKind(projectRoot)` — `.claude/settings.json` present → Claude Code; else `.kiro/` present → Kiro; neither → Claude Code (historical default, so a not-yet-installed project still reports the Claude-shaped hint). HC-1 routes to a Kiro variant (`hc1KiroHooks`) that verifies `cmk-capture.kiro.hook` + `cmk-inject.kiro.hook` and, on a miss, points at `cmk install --ide kiro` (NOT `cmk repair --hooks`). **Scope contained:** audited the other `.claude/`-touching checks — HC-6 (native Anthropic Auto Memory) checks `~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/`, an Anthropic-global feature independent of which agent the kit installed for, so it does NOT misfire on Kiro (verified PASS on the live gate project). HC-1 was the only false-fail. Test-first (3 new tests: Kiro PASS, missing-Kiro-hook FAIL with the right hint, Claude-Code-unaffected), RED→GREEN, verified live on the real `C:\Temp\kiro-gate` install (`[PASS] HC-1: Kiro IDE hooks wired`). Folded into v0.4.0 (the cut-blocker the gate exists to catch). _Relates D-184 (same separately-correct-jointly-broken class), D-182/D-183 (the Kiro surfaces doctor must now understand), the live-test discipline (this is exactly what live-testing the headline feature surfaces that unit tests can't), VD1/HC-9 (the other doctor cross-agent-adjacent check)._
- **🚧 BUILD (2026-06-21) — D-184: Kiro rework PR-2 (the CLI agent-config `hooks{}` surface + the guarded default-agent) BUILT — the 5th install surface for `kiro-cli` terminal users; the IDE hook surface (D-183) covers the GUI.** PR-2 of the D-182 rework, the follow-up D-183 flagged. **What it ships:** `kiro-cli-agent.mjs` — `installKiroCliAgent({awsDir})` writes `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/q_cli_default.json` in the **authoritative Amazon-Q Rust contract** (D-182): `hooks{agentSpawn→inject(timeout_ms:10000), stop→capture(timeout_ms:30000)}` keyed by trigger → array of `{command, timeout_ms}` (NOT the stale `agent-v1.json` `{command}`-only shape), plus `mcpServers` + a `prompt` pointing at `AGENTS.md`. The hook command is platform-correct via the shared `kiro-hook-command.mjs` (`cmd.exe /c cmk hook <event>` on Windows — the WSL-no-node finding, extracted from `kiro-ide-hooks` so BOTH surfaces share one source). **Guarded default-agent (the D-182 non-clobber rule):** a fresh install names the file `q_cli_default.json` (Kiro's auto-default convention) and reports `defaultAgent:'set'`; if the user already has a default (`chat.defaultAgent` in settings.json, OR a `q_cli_default.json` they authored), it installs a NAMED `cmk.json` instead and reports `defaultAgent:'skipped-existing'` — their default is byte-untouched. `installKiro` now wires this as the **5th surface** (`cli-agent`) and surfaces `cliDefaultAgent` so the CLI install notice can tell the user to set the default themselves when skipped. **Both hook surfaces reuse the SAME `cmk hook <event>` dispatcher** → the same `captureTurn()`/`injectContext()` core (the shared-core architecture, P-7QBE6A6M); the CLI agent-config is only another input adapter. **CRITICAL bug caught by the live-test discipline (not unit tests):** the install routing passed `options.userTier` (undefined in the real CLI) so `installKiroCliAgent` fell back to `homedir()` and wrote `q_cli_default.json` into the user's **real** `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/` during a live-check. Caught it, verified it was ours, removed it + the empty dirs, and fixed with a `MEMORY_KIT_AWS_DIR` env override + an explicit `awsDir` param — tests + live-checks ALWAYS sandbox the `~/.aws` write now (P-3Y6MCN2B). Two-pass review: self-review made the `hook` verb exit-0 explicit (`process.exitCode = 0`, I1); skill-review pending in the PR. **Honest edge (live-test rule):** the CLI agent-config + default-agent resolution + `stop`/`agentSpawn` firing in a real `kiro-cli` session is flagged for the batched manual live-test (50.M) after all v0.4.0 code lands — not claimed from unit tests. _Relates D-183 (PR-1, the IDE surface this complements — same dispatcher, forked only at the hook leg), D-182 (the settled spec: Rust contract + default-agent + the `~/.aws` path), the cross-platform rule (the shared `kiro-hook-command`), the live-test discipline (firing flagged; the `~/.aws` bug it caught), P-7QBE6A6M (shared core), P-3Y6MCN2B (the `~/.aws` sandbox rule)._
- **🚧 BUILD + 🔬 LIVE-VERIFY (2026-06-21) — D-183: Kiro rework PR-1 (shared 3 surfaces + IDE hooks) BUILT + live-verified; the IDE `.kiro.hook` surface is REINSTATED as a first-class deterministic-capture target (D-182's "IDE disqualified" was wrong).** PR-1 of the D-182 rework. **The key correction to D-182:** its "IDE `.kiro.hook` is disqualified for capture (askAgent-only)" conflated OBSERVED USAGE with CAPABILITY — the user's own Kiro-IDE-GUI-created hook is `{when:{type:agentStop}, then:{type:runCommand, command, timeout:60}}`, i.e. the IDE GUI itself emits `runCommand` on `agentStop` = **automatic deterministic capture, NO default-agent needed.** So the IDE surface is the PRIMARY target for IDE users (simpler than the CLI default-agent path); the survey repos used `askAgent` by *choice* (LLM-task-tracking), not because `runCommand` was unavailable. **What only LIVE-TESTING on the user's real Kiro could find (none of it in any doc):** (a) the `.kiro.hook` on-disk format (`{version,enabled,name,description,when:{type},then:{type:runCommand|askAgent,command|prompt,timeout}}` — docs deliberately omit it; the user's GUI hook was the only primary source); (b) **Kiro on Windows runs hook `runCommand` through WSL, and WSL has NO node** → a bare `cmk hook stop` fails (`node: not found`); the fix is **`cmd.exe /c cmk hook <event>`** (LIVE-PROVEN: a `.kiro.hook` running `cmd.exe /c cmk --version` output `0.3.5` in the Kiro chat) — emitted per-platform via the binding cross-platform rule; (c) **Kiro's hook INPUT model is argv(event) + env(`USER_PROMPT`) + cwd(project) + the transcript FILE, NOT a stdin JSON payload** like Claude Code (the probe hung on a stdin read; the AWS "Mastering Agent Hooks" article then CONFIRMED `$USER_PROMPT` + the rule that a non-zero hook exit BLOCKS the tool — hence the always-exit-0 invariant). **PR-1 ships:** `install-kiro.mjs` (the dedicated orchestrator — D-182's "Kiro needs its own installer branch") wiring 4 surfaces — MCP (`.kiro/settings/mcp.json`) + steering (`.kiro/steering/cmk.md`, `inclusion:always`) + skills (`memory-search`/`memory-write`→`.kiro/skills/`, ports 1:1) + IDE hooks (`.kiro/hooks/cmk-{capture,inject}.kiro.hook`, platform-correct command); `kiro-hook-dispatch.mjs` (router) + `kiro-hook-bin.mjs` (adapter) + the `cmk hook <event>` verb (always exit 0); `readKiroTurn` (reads the real transcript via `CONTINUE_GLOBAL_DIR` env + base64url workspace key); `managed-block.mjs` (shared marker-block + json helpers, self-review dedup). **The kit is the FIRST project to do deterministic `runCommand` memory capture on Kiro** (40+ surveyed real hooks are all `askAgent`) — which is precisely why every layer was live-verified, not copied. Two-pass review: self-review deduped `managed-block`; skill-review made exit-0 explicit (I1) + the recency tie-break deterministic (M2); the stress prerun caught a malformed `@doors` header. **Honest edge (live-test rule):** `cmk install --ide kiro` lands all 4 surfaces live-verified, and the hook *runs* (probe-proven), but the hook *firing-and-capturing-a-real-turn* end-to-end is flagged for a final manual Kiro session — not claimed from unit tests. **PR-2 (separate):** the CLI agent-config `hooks{}` surface + the guarded default-agent (for `kiro-cli` terminal users) — genuinely different files + activation from the IDE surface (the user's "cli hooks folder and ide hooks folder are not the same, right?" — correct: IDE = `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook` files; CLI = `hooks{}` inside `.kiro/agents/<name>.json`). _Relates D-182 (the spec this builds; its IDE-disqualified call corrected), D-181/D-180 (the superseded design), the cross-platform rule (the WSL `cmd.exe` finding), D-85/D-164 (deterministic auto-capture), the live-test discipline (firing flagged), the all-4-surfaces + both-surfaces decisions (P-YKG4GF25/P-F4WFAXAQ), the verified facts (P-WJRUQVSW format, P-PM2CD6CB Windows cmd, P-CJYGTQYR input model, P-XaPRJFWE AWS confirmation)._
- **🔬 RESEARCH + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-21) — D-182: the Kiro install path is SETTLED by a 14-real-project survey + the AUTHORITATIVE Amazon-Q Rust contract — and it REVISES the D-180/D-181 Kiro design on every axis. The shipped Kiro profile (D-181) is wrong against the live CLI and must be reworked before v0.4.0.** The user pushed hard + correctly: *"check more than 15 projects"* → *"if needed clone them"* → *"check actual files"* → *"the projects we checked have kiro install too?"* → *"what about steerings?"* → *"in kiro you have hooks, steerings, skills and mcp"*. Each push fixed a real error in my model. **The five corrections (all from REAL files / the Rust source, not docs):** **(1) Kiro CLI IS Amazon Q Developer CLI** — so the authoritative hook contract is the `aws/amazon-q-developer-cli` Rust source, and **the published `schemas/agent-v1.json` is a STALE SUBSET** (lists 2 triggers + `{command}`-only; the real contract has 5 triggers `agentSpawn`/`userPromptSubmit`/`preToolUse`/`postToolUse`/`stop` + `Hook{command, timeout_ms(u64 default 30000), max_output_size(10240), cache_ttl_seconds(0), matcher}`, camelCase keys). My D-180 conclusion targeted the wrong schema. **(2) The dominant real install = CLI agent-config with a `hooks{}` block** (9/14 repos; 3/4 memory repos — Auriti/kiro-memory, oh-my-kiro, vibekit), NOT the IDE `.kiro.hook` files D-180's correction had swung toward. **(3) IDE `.kiro.hook` is DISQUALIFIED for capture** — across ALL surveyed repos, ZERO use `then:runCommand` for lifecycle capture; every automatic IDE hook is `then:askAgent` (hands the LLM a prompt + hopes it calls the tool = non-deterministic) AND IDE-only (doesn't fire for `kiro-cli`). That's the exact non-determinism the kit exists to kill — so IDE hooks are OPTIONAL user-triggered convenience only, never the capture spine. **(4) Automatic activation needs the default agent** — 5/14 repos reach "fires with no `--agent` flag" by either setting `chat.defaultAgent` (2: naas, coder/registry) OR naming the agent `default`/`q_cli_default` at the user tier (3: vibekit, oh-my-kiro, Auriti). Hooks fire automatically (Rust `conversation.rs:581`) ONLY for the resolved-active agent — there is NO global hook path. So the kit MUST set the default (guarded — don't clobber a user's existing default; merge or surface a `cmk doctor` notice). The D-181 profile NEVER did this → its hooks would never auto-fire (the bug the user predicted). **(5) Kiro has FOUR surfaces, not three** (the user's correction): hooks + **steering** + **skills** + MCP. The kit's adapter omitted SKILLS entirely. Verified from real files: Kiro skills = Claude-Code-style `<name>/SKILL.md` (`.kiro/skills/` project + `~/.kiro/skills/` user — the user's own install has python-pro/systematic-debugging/…), so the kit's `memory-search`/`memory-write` skills PORT DIRECTLY. Custom **steering** with `inclusion: always` auto-loads in base mode but is DROPPED under a custom agent unless re-added via the agent's `resources:["file://.kiro/steering/<f>.md"]` (proven: 3fn/DesignerPunk's 8 agent JSONs all re-list each steering file). **THE SETTLED SPEC (D-182):** write a CLI agent-config (`q_cli_default.json` or `cmk.json`+guarded activation) to `.amazonq/cli-agents/` + `~/.aws/amazonq/cli-agents/` with `hooks{agentSpawn→'cmk hook agentSpawn'(inject, cached whole-conversation = SessionStart analog), stop→'cmk hook stop'(capture)}` (one dispatcher, usalu/semio pattern) + `mcpServers.cmk` + `resources[AGENTS.md, steering]` + `prompt:file://AGENTS.md`; PLUS the other 3 surfaces (steering `.kiro/steering/cmk.md`; skills `memory-search`/`memory-write`→`.kiro/skills/`; MCP `mcp.json`). **The user chose ALL FOUR surfaces incl. hooks** (deterministic capture, not model-compliance) + **rework Kiro PROPERLY before v0.4.0** (not ship-broken-fix-later). **8-point live-test checklist** before claiming automatic (default resolves w/o `--agent`; inject+capture FIRE not just register; non-clobber guard; MCP reachable; timeout composition). _Relates D-181 (the profile this reworks — wrong on schema/path/default-agent/skills), D-180 (the seam — its Kiro-hook conclusion superseded), D-85/D-164 (the automatic-capture thesis hooks serve), §8.5 (the `timeout_ms` composition), the all-4-surfaces + rework-now decisions (P-YKG4GF25/P-55ZLLX6T), the install-path fact (P-P9FL3NYB). Settled by a 14-project survey — do NOT re-open without new real-project evidence._

  **⚠️ CORRECTION (2026-06-21, same day) — D-182's "IDE `.kiro.hook` is DISQUALIFIED for capture (askAgent-only)" was WRONG; the IDE is a FIRST-CLASS capture target.** The user caught it: *"why are you only talking about kiro cli and not kiro ide?"* — I'd let the research collapse to CLI-only. The survey claim conflated **observed usage** with **capability**: it saw repos use `then:askAgent` (Taskmaster 7×, because their hooks are LLM-task-tracking) and concluded `runCommand` was unavailable for lifecycle events. **The user's own Kiro-IDE-UI-generated hook DISPROVES this** — it is `{when:{type:'agentStop'}, then:{type:'runCommand', command, timeout:60}}`: the IDE GUI itself emits `runCommand` on `agentStop`, i.e. **deterministic shell-command capture on turn-end, automatically, with NO default-agent needed.** So the corrected picture: **(a) Kiro IDE is the PRIMARY target** (it's the user's main work surface — the original v0.4 reason, P-DGN6ZNXZ), not a secondary convenience. **(b) BOTH surfaces support deterministic capture** — IDE via `.kiro/hooks/cmk-capture.kiro.hook` (`agentStop`→`runCommand` — automatic, simpler, no default-agent clobber risk) AND CLI via agent-config `hooks{stop}` (needs the guarded default-agent). **(c) 3 of 4 surfaces are SHARED IDE+CLI** (MCP `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` + steering `.kiro/steering/` + skills `.kiro/skills/`) — one install covers both; only the HOOKS leg forks (IDE `.kiro.hook` file vs CLI agent-config). The rest of D-182's spec stands (default-agent for the CLI side, AGENTS.md/steering/skills, Rust contract for CLI hooks); what changes is that the **IDE hook path is co-equal, not dropped** — the kit should install IDE `.kiro.hook` files for IDE users + the CLI agent-config for CLI users, sharing MCP/steering/skills. IDE hook format verified from the real file (P-WJRUQVSW): `{version:'1.0.0', enabled, name, description, when:{type}, then:{type:'runCommand', command, timeout}}`. _Relates P-WG6SMMV7 (the correction), P-WJRUQVSW (the real IDE hook format), P-N39ZJ69D (the earlier "IDE is a better fit" finding the survey wrongly overrode)._
- **🚧 BUILD + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-20) — D-181: Task 50 (cross-agent install, Kiro first) BUILT on the D-180 seam — `cmk install --ide kiro|agents-md` ships; the Kiro hook-FIRING is honestly flagged-not-claimed (one-shot CLI can't reach it).** The v0.4.0 differentiator. Built in the D-180 order — reusable spine first, then thin per-agent: **50.B `mutateAgentConfig`** (the shared config-write primitive — touch-only-our-keys, refuse-to-clobber-on-parse-error, idempotent, atomic; the one piece every agent reuses) → **50.C `defineAgentProfile`** (per-agent adapters as pure DATA validated by a factory; the integration-type taxonomy `native-hooks-mcp`/`hooks-mcp`/`mcp-only`/`instruction-only` dictates required/forbidden legs) → **50.D `validate-agent-adapter-parity`** (lint-time both-directions guard, wired into `npm test`) → **50.E Kiro profile** (CLI agent-hooks `agentSpawn`/`stop` in `.kiro/agents/cmk.json`, steering `inclusion: always`, `.kiro/settings/mcp.json`) → **50.F `--ide` routing** (`installAgent` wires a profile's 3 legs; default `claude-code` UNCHANGED — regression-verified no `.kiro`) → **50.G AGENTS.md rung** (instruction-only breadth) → **50.H** transcript parser + tests. **The Kiro transcript unknown (D-180's "highest risk") was RESOLVED to LOW by inspecting a real Kiro install** (the user: *"I have Kiro installed"*) — VS Code fork, per-session JSON at `globalStorage/kiro.kiroagent/workspace-sessions/<base64url(path)>/<sessionId>.json`, `.history[].message{role,content[].text}`; the base64url scheme verified EXACTLY (`+→-`, `/→_`, `=→_` — the `=`-padding-to-underscore detail would have been guessed wrong without the real artifact). `kiro-transcript.mjs` parses it. **LIVE-VERIFIED (real bin, sandbox):** `cmk install --ide kiro` lands all 3 legs in the verified paths in ONE step; default install unchanged; unknown agent → exit 2. **HONESTLY NOT VERIFIED (flagged, not claimed — the live-test rule):** the `agentSpawn`→inject / `stop`→capture hook FIRING in a real Kiro session — a one-shot CLI can't exercise it; it needs a manual Kiro session (the kit writes the hook entries correctly per kiro.dev docs, but "docs-correct" ≠ "fires"). **Two-pass review:** self-review caught a duplicated `atomicWrite` (deduped to a shared export); skill-review caught I1 (partial-install now reports landed legs), I2 (uninstall prunes the emptied servers/hooks husk), M1 (uninstall removes ONLY our hook events — no shared-file footgun), M4 (dropped dead parser code). Full suite 2083, stress 5/5. **Process note:** the user replaced "autopilot" with the native **`/goal`** command (verified against code.claude.com/docs/en/goal — truly hands-free, evaluator-gated; the autopilot CONTRACT became the discipline INSIDE each goal turn), and trimmed the goal's redundant `or stop after 25 turns` cap (a crisp checkable end-state + stop-on-fork is a strictly better bound than an arbitrary number). **Deferred (not blocking):** auto-detect (`~/.kiro/` → offer the agent) — the explicit `--ide` flag is the complete path; auto-detect is a UX nicety. Codex (plugin-marketplace) + Goose (YAML) out of v0.4.0 scope (highest effort, lowest reuse). _Relates D-180 (the seam this builds), D-127 (Kiro-first), D-157 (the research gate), design §16.50.1, the live-test discipline (hook-firing flagged), the `/goal` workflow fact (P-3A3PBCVB)._
- **🔬 RESEARCH + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-20) — D-180: the Task 50 cross-agent adapter research-revisit (the binding D-157 gate) ran a FULL-corpus survey + cloned-source deep-read + kiro.dev primary verification — output is the seam architecture + a load-bearing Kiro hook-system CORRECTION.** The user pushed twice to widen the lens (*"you should check more products than just this 2"* → *"please clone and check all of them"* → *"these are not the products we researched… which research are you using?"* → *"why not also do a pass on other products?"*) — the right call: my first pass leaned on only Taskmaster + claude-mem, and asserted (rather than verified) that the rest of the corpus didn't help. **Did the broad pass change the answer? NO — but it VERIFIED it instead of assuming it.** Swept all 66 research notes through the multi-agent-install lens: **only claude-mem actually installs the three legs we install (hooks + MCP + instruction-block) into multiple agents, and even it is bespoke-per-agent code, not a clean adapter.** The rest split into instruction-file-only (project-memory/GBrain/OpenClaw), MCP-connector ("multi-agent" = clients hit one running server, not an installer), a per-host-handcraft NEGATIVE example (TencentDB hand-built 2 integrations — exactly what our seam avoids), and single-agent/core-only (mem0/Letta/Zep/memsearch/mempalace/memory-os/OpenHands/AgentCore/…). So most of our corpus shaped the kit's CORE, not the adapter — which is WHY the adapter corpus was genuinely thin (now confirmed, not guessed). **THREE load-bearing findings:** (1) **Don't build a uniform `Installer` base class** — claude-mem proved it breaks the moment agents differ in format (Goose YAML, Codex TOML) or mechanism (Cursor whole-file vs Gemini surgical-merge vs Codex plugin-marketplace). The reusable seam is a shared, TESTED `mutateAgentConfig(path, format, keyPath, entry, {merge|replace})` primitive (touch-only-our-keys, refuse-to-clobber-on-parse-error, idempotent `changed`-boolean) + per-agent metadata as **DATA, not classes** — which maps onto the kit's existing marker-block byte-preservation + over-mutation-guard rules. Do NOT registry-ize the matrix yet (single-digit N; opencode's registry pays off at N≈75). (2) **🔴 Kiro has TWO hook systems and only ONE fits (primary-verified correction).** Target **Kiro CLI agent-hooks** — `agentSpawn` (=SessionStart-inject) + `stop` (=turn-end-capture), defined inside `.kiro/agents/<name>.json` — NOT the IDE "Agent Hooks" surface (file-event-centric, no documented session-start trigger, no documented on-disk format). **The Taskmaster `.kiro/hooks/*.kiro.hook` claim was the WRONG hook system** (the §5.1 convergent-third-party-≠-primary precedent, caught exactly as the rule predicts). Good news: the kit's inject-at-start/capture-at-end model PORTS CLEANLY to the CLI surface. Steering → `.kiro/steering/` (`inclusion: always`); MCP → `.kiro/settings/mcp.json` (`mcpServers`) — both primary-verified. (3) **Highest UNVERIFIED risk: Kiro's transcript format is unknown.** The kit's extract/compress hardcodes Claude-Code touchpoints (`~/.claude/projects/<slug>/<session>.jsonl`, `env -u CLAUDECODE`); kiro.dev docs don't cover Kiro's transcript-on-disk shape → must be parameterized per-agent + discovered LIVE at build (the capture half of the model gates on it). **Build order (the note's §6):** `mutateAgentConfig` primitive FIRST (+ over-mutation test) → per-agent profile data-shape → adapter-parity validator → Kiro profile → AGENTS.md breadth rung → `cmk install --ide` routing → live verification (hook-firing + transcript format flagged for a real Kiro session, NOT claimed verified from docs). Output committed as [research note `2026-06-20-cross-agent-adapter-seam-task50.md`](../research/2026-06-20-cross-agent-adapter-seam-task50.md); facts captured via `cmk remember` (P-AGV23NTY/P-SAX2JDHY/P-RT2G5VAY). **Meta-lesson: the user's "check more than 2 / clone all / which research?" forced the full-corpus verification that turned "the adapter corpus is thin" from an assumption into a verified finding — and the cloned-source read is what surfaced the don't-build-a-base-class lesson a docs-only survey would have missed.** _Relates D-157 (the research-revisit gate this satisfies), D-127 (Kiro-first), ADR-0012 (cross-agent future), design §16.49/§16.50, Task 50 (the build this feeds), the §5.1 primary-source precedent (the Kiro hook-system correction is a textbook instance), the live-test discipline (hook-firing + transcript flagged, not claimed)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-19) — D-175: Task 161's fix is a BOUNDED, TRANSIENT-ONLY RETRY — grounded in a full-field code read (9 systems), placed only on the ceiling-free paths. The plan was RE-ESTABLISHED after winging it (the user: "this is getting out of hand… read the code, all of it, then go back to research, and then restart the task with an established and well thought out plan").** After D-174 inverted the size-bound design to a retry, I (a) read the WHOLE compression subsystem end-to-end (compress-session / compressor / lazy-compress / session-end-tasks / daily-distill / weekly-curate / the bins), and (b) read how the field ACTUALLY retries — not 1 system (the first pass tunneled on OpenHands; the user: "why only OpenHands?" / "only 6?"), but **9 systems' real retry code** → [retry-patterns research note](../research/2026-06-19-llm-call-retry-patterns-cross-system.md). **Unanimous convergence (7 of 7 retrying systems):** bounded attempts (2–4), backoff (exponential majority / linear memclaw), **retry ONLY the transient class (rate-limit / 5xx / timeout / empty-response) keyed on the error TYPE, NEVER the deterministic class (4xx / context-length / policy-violation / ENOENT), reraise after exhaustion.** graphiti's `is_server_or_retry_error` predicate + Letta's `ValueError`(retry)-vs-`RuntimeError`(don't) split are the model. **Decisive negative result:** **claude-remember — the precedent the kit's compress was COPIED from — does NOT retry** (single attempt, raises `RuntimeError`, moves on); claude-mem doesn't either. So the kit inherited the *no-retry* gap from its precedents, exactly as it inherited the unbounded-input gap (D-174). **THE PLAN (Task 161.8–161.11):** a `compressWithRetry(backend, opts, {maxAttempts≤2, baseBackoffMs, isRetryable})` helper — `isRetryable` true for `HaikuTimeoutError` + a transient `HaikuFailedError` (classified via the `exitCode`/`stderr` that 161.6a now captures — this is WHY observability shipped first), false for ENOENT / deterministic exit. **Placement keyed to the verified composition budgets:** the CEILING-FREE paths (`dailyDistill`, `weeklyCurate`, the detached lazy `compressSession`) get the retry; the **SessionEnd-hook `compressSession` gets NONE** — it runs under the 60s ceiling CONCURRENT with `autoPersona` (D-42) where a 50s attempt + 50s retry = 100s blows the ceiling, so it keeps its existing restore-on-failure (D-79) and DELEGATES the retry to the now-retrying lazy path one session later (the field's "two valid placements" — explicit loop vs delegate). **REOPENED items from the set-aside D-173:** input-capping (A) is NOT in the plan (D-174 falsified its premise); it returns only if a future huge-buffer case is ever measured. _Relates D-174 (the inversion that made this a retry problem), D-173 (the set-aside size-bound), D-79 (restore-on-failure — the hook path's delegated-retry mechanism), D-42 (the 60s concurrent ceiling that bars an in-hook retry), 161.6a (the observability fix the transient/deterministic classification depends on), §8.5 (timeout/ceiling composition), the [retry research note](../research/2026-06-19-llm-call-retry-patterns-cross-system.md) + the [19-system note](../research/2026-06-18-session-buffer-compaction-under-latency-growth.md). The user's process correction (read-all-code → re-research → re-plan) is itself the lesson: don't improvise a design mid-conversation — establish it from the code + the field first._
- **🐛 BUG + FIX (2026-06-20) — D-179: the ceiling-free compress callers used the hook-sized 50s timeout → needless `haiku_timeout` → `recent.md` went 4 days stale on the dogfood repo (Task 163, fixed).** Surfaced live: after the Claude Code + cmk update, `cmk doctor` HC-2 showed `recent.md` 4d stale. **The user's instinct was the catch — "if it's not automatic, it's a bug"** — and stopped me from papering over it with a manual `cmk daily-distill`. **Investigated with real data** (not guessed): the daily-distill INPUT is tiny (4.7 KB), yet it timed out at 50s; a measurement of the REAL input showed `claude --print` taking **18–27s when fast but 78s in a slow window** — pure ENVIRONMENTAL slowness (confirms D-174: not size-driven), and the slow window can be SUSTAINED, so the v0.3.4 retry (50s + 50s, both inside the same slow window) didn't help. **Root cause:** `daily-distill`, `weekly-curate`'s curate call, and the lazy `compressSession` all used `timeoutMs: 50_000` — the value sized for the **60s SessionEnd HOOK ceiling** — despite being **CEILING-FREE** (cron / detached-lazy children with NO outer ceiling). The D-92/F-2 composition rule (a ceiling-free caller must NOT inherit a ceiling-sized bound) was applied to `weekly-curate`'s PERSONA call (120s) but MISSED on the other three. The v0.3.4 retry comment itself said "ceiling-free path" while the timeout stayed 50s. **FIX (Task 163):** the three ceiling-free sites → **120s** (matching weekly-curate's persona call); `compressSession` gains a `timeoutMs` param (default 50s = the hook contract; the lazy caller passes 120s) — mirrors the `maxAttempts` param. **Composition VERIFIED:** the lazy child is `detached:true` + unref'd, so the 120s×2≈240s worst case runs in the BACKGROUND after the 30s SessionStart hook returns — no ceiling violation; cron is standalone; the SessionEnd-hook `compressSession` keeps 50s (it HAS the 60s ceiling). **LIVE-PROVEN on the real stale repo:** the patched daily-distill ran the real input in **77.9s** (would have died at 50s, succeeded at 120s) and `recent.md` refreshed. Full suite 2029/2029. **Secondary finding (filed, NOT fixed here):** on a busy cron-less repo the lazy cascade can ALSO starve daily/recent — `now.md` keeps refilling → verdict stays `stale-now` → rarely advances to `stale-daily`; the DESIGNED mitigation is `cmk register-crons` (HC-5 was SKIP on this repo). **Process note (mine):** I initially mis-diagnosed this as cascade-starvation, then as an input-size issue — the real-data measurement (78s on 4.7KB) corrected both to "ceiling-free timeout mis-sized"; the user's "dig deeper" + "it's a bug if not automatic" forced the measurement over the guess. **▶ SECOND LEVER — the BACKOFF was also misconfigured (the user's two follow-ups: "escalating timeout?" then "backoff tuning?").** Checked the escalating-timeout idea against **19 cloned systems** — **NONE escalate the per-attempt timeout; ALL use a fixed timeout + exponential backoff BETWEEN attempts** (graphiti `wait_random_exponential(min=5,max=120)`, Letta cap 10s, mempalace `2**attempt`s — all in SECONDS). So escalation was rejected (no prior art, adds cost for no measured gain). **But the field-check surfaced a real bug:** the kit's `compressWithRetry` backoff default is **600 MILLISECONDS** — the field waits 5–120 SECONDS. D-174's slowness is a transient WINDOW; a 600ms backoff retries INSIDE the same slow window, so attempt 2 hits the same slowness. **FIX (added to Task 163):** a `CEILING_FREE_BACKOFF_MS = 5_000` constant (field low-end) on the ceiling-free retrying paths so a retry lands AFTER the window; `compressSession` gains a `baseBackoffMs` param (default 600ms; lazy caller passes 5s). Both timeout (120s) + backoff (5s) extracted to named constants in `compress-retry.mjs` so the family can't drift back. Safe on every path (hook = maxAttempts:1, backoff never fires; ceiling-free = detached/cron, a 5s wait is free). **Meta-lesson: the user's "don't check just one, check at least 15" forced the broad survey that both KILLED the escalation idea AND found the backoff bug — a single-system check would have missed both.** _Relates D-174/D-175 (the retry this complements — retry handles a blip, the right BUDGET handles a sustained slow call, the right BACKOFF lands the retry after the window), D-92/F-2 (the ceiling-free-timeout composition rule this completes across the family), §8.5 (timeout policy), Task 105/D-75 (the lazy-cascade-starvation secondary finding), HC-5 (cron — the designed mitigation), the 19-system retry research (escalation rejected, backoff-too-short found)._

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-19) — D-176: Task 162 (update path) ships as DOCS + a `cmk doctor` drift-check (HC-9), NOT a `cmk update` command — scoped by "best, easy user experience," not by the tier list.** D-172 filed the gap (the user: "what do users do if they want to update… there is no documented or guided way"). The user reframed the scope question from "how much code" to *"what gives the user the best, easiest update experience?"* — and asked to SEE the step-by-step before deciding. The answer: the painful part of both routes is the **easily-forgotten per-project re-stamp** (update the global package/plugin, then re-run `cmk install` / `bootstrap` in each project), and the kit was silent about it. So the best experience = **(1) clear docs for both routes + (2) the kit TELLS you when a project is behind** (the drift-check), WITHOUT building a `cmk update` command that would only help the npm route and would shell into the user's `npm install -g` (a system-level action). **SHIPPED:** **(a)** "Updating to a new version" in README + QUICKSTART §9 — npm two-step + plugin flow, both VERIFIED against primary docs (the `/plugin update` behavior was checked via the claude-code-guide agent, NOT assumed: `/plugin marketplace update` → `/plugin update` → `/reload-plugins` → re-`bootstrap` per project; third-party marketplace has no auto-update; bootstrap re-scaffold is undocumented upstream so the kit documents its own per-project re-run); the Windows EBUSY-close-Claude-Code note. **(b) `cmk doctor` HC-9** — a pure `checkVersionDrift({claudeMdText, kitVersion})` (`version-drift.mjs`) compares the project's CLAUDE.md `:start vX` marker against `getKitVersion()`: FAIL + `cmk install` when the binary is newer (the forgotten step), PASS on match or a benign downgrade (older global cli, newer scaffold — not drift), SKIP when no managed block. Reuses `findManagedBlock` + `compareVersions` (exported from claude-md.mjs — shared-module discipline, not re-implemented). Live-tested on the real bin (stale project → HC-9 FAIL with the exact re-install message). **DEFERRED (deliberately, as not-necessary):** a `cmk update` command + an npm-outdated network check — the docs + drift-detection deliver the experience; a wrapper that runs `npm install -g` for the user is convenience over a now-documented 2-step, and reaches into the user's global install. **The existing `cmk-version-check` Setup-hook stub stays "not yet implemented"** — HC-9 is the on-demand doctor surface; a session-start drift NUDGE (filling that stub) is a separate future call, not bundled here. _Provenance: D-172 (the gap), the user's "best easy experience" reframe + "show me the step-by-step" + "is it really necessary? docs+drift-check now." Relates Task 162, Task 73 (the stale-scaffold-CONTENT refresh — the other half), the install version-stamping, D-80 (EBUSY), the claude-code-guide /plugin-update verification, the cmk-version-check stub (plugin/bin)._
- **🔬 MEASUREMENT + ↩️ PIVOT (2026-06-19) — D-174: the compress timeout is ENVIRONMENTAL, NOT input-size-driven — which INVERTS D-173's A/C-as-core premise. Investigation-first paid off (the user: "investigate the discrepancy first").** Before implementing A+C (bound the input size), measured real Haiku latency — and the data falsifies the size-driven premise: **(a)** a fresh harness ran 2 KB→200 KB in a flat **12–18s, three runs, zero size correlation, nothing near 50s**; **(b)** the kit's OWN `compress.log` (12 real entries) shows timeouts spanning **8 KB–334 KB** and successes spanning **229 B–470 KB — the largest SUCCESS (470 KB, 21s) is BIGGER than the largest timeout (334 KB)**; a 9 KB input timed out while 470 KB succeeded. **There is no relationship between input size and timeout.** The "compounding size spiral" framing in D-171/D-173 is therefore wrong AS STATED: a growing buffer does NOT make timeouts more likely (470 KB succeeds in 21s); the buffer grows only because a failed all-or-nothing compress leaves it un-drained, but the failure itself is size-independent. **Two failure modes in the log, NEITHER size-driven:** `haiku_timeout` (`claude --print` intermittently slow — plausibly transient/environmental) and `compress_failed` (subprocess non-zero exit — e.g. the 14:21 pair: 470 KB SUCCEEDED at 14:21:04, then a 329-byte input FAILED 19s later). **HONEST RETRACTION:** I first labeled the 329-byte failure "EBUSY/contention class" — that was a GUESS dressed as a finding (EBUSY is an unrelated Windows file-lock error; the real reason was unknowable because **the compressor captured the subprocess stderr+exit-code and then DISCARDED them — the log kept only `error_category`**). **CONSEQUENCE FOR THE DESIGN:** A (input cap) would NOT have prevented a single failure in the log (the 8 KB / 9 KB / 329-byte failures are already tiny) — so **A+C as the CORE fix is set aside** (kept in the trail per decision-trail rule; A may survive as a trivial guard). The real fix direction is **retry/robustness on a transient failure (the old "D")** — BUT only if `compress_failed` is actually transient, which we couldn't confirm because the WHY was discarded. **DECISION: fix the observability gap FIRST (done this session, test-first) — `HaikuFailedError` now carries structured `exitCode`+`stderr`, and all three compress callers (compress-session/daily-distill/weekly-curate) write `exit_code`+`error_detail` into compress.log** (live-verified: a real non-zero exit logs `exit_code:9` + the stderr). So the NEXT `compress_failed` is diagnosable, and the retry-vs-deterministic-failure question can be answered from real data instead of a guess. **The A/B/C/D design (D-173) is NOT yet re-settled** — it's reopened by this measurement; re-decide once a few real failures carry their reasons. _Relates D-171 (the spiral framing this corrects), D-173 (the A/C premise this inverts — set aside, not deleted), Task 161 (161.6 measurement done; the fix direction is now retry-not-cap, pending diagnosable failures), §8.5 (the timeout policy), the live-test + "investigate don't guess" disciplines (this is the textbook case — measuring falsified the premise before code shipped), the lazy-framing rule (the "EBUSY/contention" guess was exactly the lazy-framing class, self-caught)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-18) — D-173: the compress-session timeout spiral is fixed by BOUNDING THE INPUT, not raising the timeout (Task 161 design, v0.3.4). Settled by a 19-system fresh-clone survey.** _**SET ASIDE 2026-06-19 by D-174 (above) — the A/C-as-core premise (size-driven latency) was FALSIFIED by measurement; preserved here per the decision-trail rule. The 19-system "bound the input" survey + the four-family taxonomy remain valid prior art; what changed is that OUR failure is environmental, not size-driven, so input-capping isn't the core fix for US.**_ Task 161's RESEARCH-FIRST phase (D-171) ran: cloned + re-derived from CURRENT source (NOT prior notes — the user: *"repos could change, research again"*; *"are you sure this is all… did you try mempalace / TencentDB / caura-memclaw?"*; *"did you clone and check claude-remember?"*) **19 memory/agent systems** → [research note](../research/2026-06-18-session-buffer-compaction-under-latency-growth.md). **The finding: 17 of 19 systems BOUND their compaction input before the LLM call; the only 2 that DON'T are exactly the kit's own precedents** — `claude-remember` (still unbounded, survives on a 120s timeout + daily-delta staging — the "raise the timeout" approach, used as a *primary* fix by NO ONE) and `claude-mem` (which has SINCE moved to per-turn last-message, abandoning the whole-buffer shape). The kit inherited the antipattern from these two and never added the bound the rest of the field (incl. both direct competitors memsearch + caura-memclaw) treats as table-stakes. **The re-clone caught a stale-note error:** my first draft (from the old 2026-05-21 surveys) claimed claude-mem AND claude-remember share the spiral as-currently-shaped — fresh reads corrected both (claude-mem moved on; claude-remember is unbounded but hides it behind 120s). **Provenance:** the ORIGIN research note ([2026-05-21-claude-ai-deep-research-option-b.md](../research/2026-05-21-claude-ai-deep-research-option-b.md), line 437) already specified the guard — *"if Haiku compression latency routinely > 3 s p95 → drop the rolling window"* — a 3s budget written at design time, never wired in; we're now at 21–89s. **Task 161 closes a guard the original design called for and the build dropped.** **DECISION (the adopted mechanism set, design §8.2.5) — REFINED 2026-06-18 by a product-design review (the user: *"according to our research AND our kit's own design, as a product"*).** The first draft proposed A+B+C+D bolted onto `now.md`; reading the kit's OWN code + tenets collapsed it to **A+C at one shared seam, B dropped, D deferred** — and the refinement IS the decision: **(CORE) A+C in a shared `boundCompressionInput(input, {keepRecent})` helper the THREE verbs call right before `backend.compress()`** — keep the most-recent slice verbatim (C, snapped to a `## <ts> —` turn / `## <date>` day delimiter) + hard-cap the total to `COMPRESS_INPUT_CAP_BYTES` (A); the older overflow is safe to summarize-or-drop because `now.md`/`today-*.md` are **DERIVED buffers over the durable transcripts/recent/archive tiers** (the full raw turn is in `context/transcripts/` first — verified in capture-turn). **Placement: a shared HELPER the verbs call, NOT inside `CompressorBackend.compress`** — "what's recent" is verb-specific (turn boundary vs day boundary), so policy stays with the verb, backend stays a dumb transport. **(D, priority GATED on an open question — NOT cleanly deferred):** `minimum_progress` floor + shrink-and-retry on `haiku_timeout`. The cut-gate data is ambiguous on whether the latency is INPUT-SIZE-driven (big inputs 166–470 KB timed out → A fixes it) or ENVIRONMENTAL (a ~10 KB buffer took 71–89s → A does NOT fix that — a capped small input can still time out on a slow-Haiku moment and never drain). If environmental, D is part of the CORE, not defense-in-depth. **RESOLVE at implementation by measuring real Haiku latency vs input size; if noisy, D ships WITH A (at least a single bounded retry).** Treat as core-pending until measured. **(B, DROPPED for v0.3.4 — reason IS in the code):** the first draft's PostToolUse mid-session drain was to stop `now.md` growing unbounded. But `compress-session.mjs` `claimNowBuffer` ALREADY drains `now.md` fully on every successful compress (it `renameSync`-es the whole file away → compresses → discards; all-or-nothing). So `now.md`'s growth is NOT a missing-drain problem — it's "the all-or-nothing compress keeps TIMING OUT so the existing drain never runs." Fix the timeout (A+C) and the existing claim-rename drains `now.md` to empty again — nothing left for B to solve. A mid-session hook would fix a problem the existing drain already handles (memsearch has none either). Reconsider only if live data shows `now.md` bloats EVEN WHEN compresses succeed. **Four product-coherence points the review surfaced:** (1) the spiral is at the COMPRESS-CALL SEAM not one file — a `now.md`-only cap just MOVES it to `today-*.md` (the user's catch; `dailyDistill`'s `readBuffer` VERIFIED to have the identical unbounded shape today); (2) trimming the derived buffer's oldest loses nothing (durable copy in transcripts/recent/archive); (3) keep-recent-verbatim ADVANCES the Task-84 faithfulness Hard Rules (zero hallucination on the freshest content), not just latency; (4) input-side only ⇒ the ≤10 KB frozen-snapshot budget (§7) is untouched (output already `maxOutputBytes`-capped). Reuses the kit's OWN `NOW_MD_ASSISTANT_CAP` precedent. **Fires:** SessionStart-lazy + SessionEnd rolls stay AS-IS (no new drain — the seam-bound makes the EXISTING SessionEnd placement reliable under the D-42 60s ceiling). **Covers the whole family** (binding, cut-gate-16 §7 F-4): all three verbs (compress-session, daily-distill, weekly-curate) wrap `boundCompressionInput`. **REJECTED:** candidate (d) raise-the-timeout (zero of 19 use it as a primary fix; claude-remember's 120s is the living proof — bigger budget, same unbounded shape); abolishing the buffer for per-turn (the offline batch rollup is a deliberate cost choice; auto-extract is already the per-turn layer); and (the review's own pivot) the A+B+C+D-everywhere first draft (B is redundant once A+C bind the seam — preserved here per the decision-trail rule). _Implementation is test-first NEXT. Relates Task 161, D-171 (the filing this designs), Task 84 (OpenHands shrink-retry already noted), Task 105/D-75 (the unbounded-now.md class), §8.2.5 (the design write-up), §8.5 (timeout/ceiling composition), §16.27 (the mid-session cap site), D-42 (concurrent SessionEnd budget). The 19-system research note + the 2026-05-21 origin note (the dropped 3s guard)._

The actual path is undocumented + two-step + non-obvious: (1) `npm install -g @lh8ppl/claude-memory-kit@latest`, (2) re-run `cmk install` **per project** to refresh the version-stamped scaffold (CLAUDE.md block / hooks / skills / gitattributes all carry `:start vX` markers), (3) restart Claude Code. Updating the npm package ALONE doesn't update a project. **Dogfood proof (not hypothetical) — bit us twice this session:** the stale global binary (+ a stale tarball that nearly shipped the wrong code), and the stale/missing scaffolded skills until `cmk install` re-ran; plus the Windows EBUSY locked-DLL gotcha that can fail the npm update itself while Claude Code is running. **DECISION:** Task 162, v0.3.4 (within-paradigm polish). Tiered scope: MINIMUM = document the update flow (README/QUICKSTART) + a `cmk doctor` line; BETTER = a `cmk update` command + a doctor version-drift HC. - **🐛 ISSUE + DECISION (2026-06-18) — D-171: session-buffer compression times out as `now.md` grows → a compounding degradation spiral → Task 161, v0.3.4, RESEARCH-FIRST.** The v0.3.3 cut-gate-16 D6 gate (SessionStart self-heal) FAILED: the now→today roll errored `haiku_timeout`. **Investigated properly (not guessed):** isolated the `claude --print` spawn (plain `say OK` → <30s, so the CLI is alive, NOT nested-claude, NOT env-broken — an earlier guess I had to correct); ran the EXACT compressor invocation (`--print --model claude-haiku-4-5 --tools "" --max-turns 1 --mcp-config {"mcpServers":{}} --strict-mcp-config --output-format text`) with the real ~10 KB buffer → **71s then 89s** on two consecutive runs, producing a CORRECT 4-section summary — so the compression LOGIC is fine; `claude --print` Haiku latency simply exceeds the **50s** inner timeout (`compress-session.mjs:334`). **The spiral (the user's load-bearing insight):** a failed roll leaves `now.md` UNTOUCHED (fail-safe) and retries **only at the next SessionStart** (cooldown-on-success-only) — so the buffer keeps GROWING, each compression input gets BIGGER, takes LONGER, hits 50s more, grows more. **It correlates, and it's already happening on the kit's OWN repo:** `context/sessions/*.compress.log` shows real compressions 21s–50s+, **5 historical timeouts**, and `now.md` inputs that reached **166/334/405/470 KB** (all timed out). This re-instances the Task-105/D-75 unbounded-`now.md` class, gated behind a timeout instead of a missing hook. **DECISION:** NOT a v0.3.3 blocker (v0.3.3's shipped features — journal recall/auto-sync/tombstone/Bug-1 — are all deterministic, no model, verified clean; the journal-sync in the same failed lazy run logged fine). It's a real, GROWING problem → **Task 161, v0.3.4** (within-paradigm polish patch — not v0.4.0, which is reserved for the Kiro differentiator). **RESEARCH-FIRST is binding (the user: "real deep research, not just skim over"):** clone + read how squad/basic-memory/mem0/MemoryOS/Letta/claude-mem/OpenHands handle session-buffer compaction under latency+growth (incremental/chunked? compress-at-session-END too? buffer cap + compress-overflow? deterministic pre-trim? shrink-and-retry?) BEFORE designing the fix. The user's own hunch (compress at session-END too, so SessionStart rarely faces a huge backlog) is a candidate, not the decision. _Relates Task 161 (the task), Task 84 (compression §8 — OpenHands shrink-and-retry/KEEP_FIRST already noted), Task 105/D-75 (unbounded-now.md), §8.5 (timeout/hook-ceiling composition), D-42 (concurrent compress+persona under 60s). The cut-gate-16 finding._

- **🔧 FIX + NOTE (2026-06-18) — Task 159 BUILT; two implementation pivots off the D-169 plan, recorded for the trail.** Task 159 (auto-sync `DECISIONS.md`) is implemented on branch `task-159-auto-sync-decision-journal` (unit-green, live-tested: capture→session-end→journal-with-no-`cmk digest`; delete→fallback-lazy→rebuilt; forget→re-sync→retracted-in-place `_(retracted 2026-06-18)_`). Two pivots off D-169's traced seams, both documented in the [squad research note](../research/2026-06-18-squad-decision-journal-auto-maintenance.md) "Implementation divergences" section + design §8.2.4: **(1)** the SessionStart fallback uses a **standalone `isJournalStale()` boolean**, NOT a `journal-stale` verdict in `detectStaleness` (D-169 + the research traced the verdict) — because `detectStaleness` returns ONE verdict and `runLazyCompress` dispatches ONE compress stage, so a competing journal verdict would SUPPRESS compress work (the separately-correct-jointly-broken composition class); the boolean keeps compress-staleness and journal-staleness orthogonal (`inject-context` OR-s them; `runLazyCompress` syncs the journal unconditionally). **(2)** `isJournalStale` compares **`context/memory/INDEX.md` mtime** (O(1) proxy — `write-fact` rewrites it on every fact write), NOT "the newest `type:project` fact" mtime — a self-review find: the literal "newest fact" needed a `statSync` per file = **~130ms on the 307-fact dogfood corpus**, growing linearly, and `isJournalStale` runs inline on EVERY SessionStart (the 500ms NFR-1 budget). The O(1) proxy accepts one trade-off: INDEX covers all fact types, so a feedback-only write can flag the journal stale → one spurious detached sync (idempotent, ~175ms, never a correctness issue). **v0.3.3 tag-blocker status:** Task 159 lands the auto-sync; DJ5 (no-`cmk digest` gate) + the retracted-on-real-data path were live-verified this session. _Relates D-169 (the plan these pivot from), the research note (divergences recorded), design §8.2.4, the composition rules (the WHY behind pivot 1), the live-test rule (pivot 2 surfaced in self-review/perf-measure)._
