This also made DJ4-live untestable in a fresh project (no journal → `--scope decisions` returns `[]`, the AI answers from facts and masks it — exactly what cut-gate-15 showed across two live runs). **Research (squad, the SOURCE project — kept at `/c/tmp/squad-dive` per the user):** squad keeps `decisions.md` current via an agent **inbox drop-box** + a dedicated **"Scribe" LLM agent** that merges inbox→`decisions.md` at a **session-end ceremony**. **DECISION — deterministic-on-hook, NOT an LLM Scribe:** the kit's journal is **deterministically derivable from the already-captured structured `type:project` facts** (squad needs an LLM Scribe because its decisions are unstructured prose; the kit's are typed facts), so it just runs the deterministic `syncDecisionsJournal` (~175ms, pure file I/O, no Haiku) on a hook — better than the source. **Placement (seams traced):** primary = the detached SESSION-END path (`runSessionEndTasks`, a 3rd sequential local-I/O step beside the graduation sweep — the exact pure-file-I/O/`<<1s`/wrapped template at lines 61-76); fallback = a `journal-stale` verdict in `detectStaleness` (SessionStart lazy path, for no-clean-exit sessions, detached, never blocks the 500ms budget) — mirroring the §8.2.1/8.2.2 lazy-compress precedent. **v0.3.3 does NOT tag until Task 159 + the DJ4 re-test land** — the DECISIONS.md feature isn't "it just works" (D-164) until the journal auto-populates. _Relates Task 147 (the "made automatic" intent), Task 156 (recall — the half we DID finish), D-161 (append-only model), D-164 (automatic-or-not-shipped), squad (the source mechanism), §8.2.1/8.2.2 (lazy-compress), §19.4.2 (recall). Fact P-UCG4RKNL-adjacent (the cut-gate session)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-16) — D-166: Bug 2 (stale version in the SessionStart snapshot) is a fact-currency instance — DEFER to the Task 66 → Task 95 chain, do NOT special-case it.** A fresh session's injected snapshot said "v0.3.1 shipped / v0.3.2 deferred" AFTER v0.3.2 shipped (the user: "what happens if I start a new session?"). **Root cause (corrected from the bug's first framing):** the snapshot injects `MEMORY.md` + the latest `today-*.md` — NOT `recent.md` — and the stale "v0.3.2 deferred" line sat in `MEMORY.md`/`today-*.md` because **nothing superseded it when the ship happened** (auto-extract ADDs facts; it doesn't mark an existing fact stale on a later contradiction). So the 2026-06-16 interim fix that appended to `recent.md` never actually reached the snapshot — it worked by luck (a later auto-extract overwrote `MEMORY.md`), which itself proved the framing was off. **The decision turned on a doc + research check the user forced** (their questions "task 95 fixes this bug? is this a cheap substitute? do you need deep research / doc check / project check?"): (1) **Task 95 IS scoped to fix this** — it's the mem0-style batched ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NONE contradiction-resolve (D-73), and its OWN headline example is "moved Postgres→SQLite as a supersede, not a contradicting ADD" — version state is the identical shape; (2) the research (Chandra "Beyond the Log", §16.18) treats *current status* as a **Current-State temporal-validity fact** ("what is X now?" → boost `status: ongoing`), and **no researched memory system computes status as a config field**; (3) sequencing is **Task 66 (validity windows) BEFORE Task 95** (memsearch/MemPalace dive — the assert-vs-window check needs windows first). **REJECTED Option C** (a deterministic "project status" pin computed from `package.json` + `CHANGELOG`): it would fix only the version line via a carve-out mechanism the prior art doesn't use — routing around the real currency model rather than building it. **DECISION:** no special v0.3.3 Bug-2 fix; Bug 2 folds into the Task 66→95 chain (fixes version state AND the whole Current-State staleness class generally); the interim hand-fix holds and the narrow residual window (a major event between the event and the next capture/curate) is acceptable until then. _Fact P-UCG4RKNL (Bug 2 half). Relates Bug 1 / D-165 (same fact, shipped), Task 66 (validity windows), Task 95 (re-curation contradiction-resolve, D-62/D-73), §16.18 + §8.0 (the currency gap), §8.2.3 (the design write-up), the "Beyond the Log" research note._
- **🐛 BUG + FIX (2026-06-16) — D-165: `cmk reindex --full` crashed `UNIQUE constraint failed: observations.id` on the kit's own corpus — file-keyed DELETE against an id-keyed PRIMARY KEY (fixed, v0.3.3 branch).** Surfaced when the user asked "what happens if I start a new session?" / "do we have a bug?" The kit's `cmk remember` **dual-writes** a fact to BOTH the `context/MEMORY.md` Active-Threads bullet AND its granular `context/memory/<type>_*.md` archive file — **both carrying the same content-addressed id**. But `observations.id` is a global `PRIMARY KEY` and `replaceObservationsForFile` deleted by `source_file` only; so when reindex processed the second source holding that id, the INSERT collided and aborted the WHOLE reindex (reproduced deterministically: 4 colliding ids on the live corpus — P-TLTURYF7 / ZVQEMWJA / F94ZJMYV / 7Q5U4XTK). **Root-cause research (full cross-project pass, NOT recall — the user pushed: "did you do a full research… clone to disk… articles… deep research online?"):** cloned + read the storage/index code of TencentDB-Agent-Memory, **basic-memory** (the closest design twin: markdown=truth, SQLite=index), memweave (markdown+SQLite+sqlite-vec), claude-memory-compiler, obsidian-index-service, sqlite-memory, memsearch + a web pass on the SQLite canon. **Three independent markdown-first analogs converge on one rule: key replacement on the id/content, keep ONE logical row per id, never a composite `(id, file)` key** — TencentDB upserts by `record_id` (`ON CONFLICT(record_id) DO UPDATE`); basic-memory keeps one file per permalink via `resolve_permalink` disambiguation + a *partial* unique index; memweave dedups by content-hash. None of the kit's predecessors (claude-remember/project-memory/claude-mem) hit this because none combined a rolling-window scratchpad WITH a stable-id per-fact archive — the collision is the kit's own. (Research note: [`docs/research/2026-06-16-index-uniqueness-id-vs-file-scoped-delete.md`](../research/2026-06-16-index-uniqueness-id-vs-file-scoped-delete.md).) **FIX:** id-keyed replacement with deterministic **archive-beats-scratchpad precedence** in `replaceObservationsForFile` — a `fact`-kind source does explicit `DELETE FROM observations WHERE id = ?` then INSERT (always wins, archive = the canonical Why/How home); a `scratchpad`-kind source does `INSERT … ON CONFLICT(id) DO NOTHING` (yields if a row already exists). Order-INDEPENDENT: whichever is walked first, the fact row survives, pointing at the granular archive. **Self-review caught a second bug before merge:** the first impl used `INSERT OR REPLACE` for the fact path — but `observations_fts` is an external-content FTS5 table whose only safe delete is the `obs_after_delete` 'delete' sentinel; `INSERT OR REPLACE` reuses the rowid and **orphaned the old scratchpad body in the FTS index** (kept MATCH-ing with no backing row — silent stale-hit corruption). A strengthened Door-4 test (`MATCH 'scratchpad'` → 0; `ftsCount == obsCount`) failed, exposing it; switched to explicit DELETE-by-id (fires the sentinel cleanly). Live-verified on the real corpus: no crash, FTS consistent (290 obs = 290 fts), all 4 dups → one archive row. Fact P-UCG4RKNL. _Relates Bug 2 (snapshot staleness, same P-UCG4RKNL, still open for v0.3.3), ADR-0002 (markdown-truth + rebuildable index), ADR-0009 (per-observation ids), design §9.2 (reindex)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-16) — D-164: DECISIONS.md / `cmk digest` HELD for v0.3.3 — a feature isn't shipped until it works end-to-end (write AND automatic AI-recall).** The cut-gate surfaced that the Task-147 decision journal is **write-only for the AI** (not in any recall directive, not indexed — D-JYH2P5QC gap). The user's decisive reframe: *"this feature is actually NOT for the human to go and read the file himself — most users will not do that. They'll think it's automatic like the rest of the kit: you ask the AI and it recalls the decisions, timeline, why and when. The work-for-human is just a stop-gap, not the actual solution."* That's the kit's whole thesis (D-85: you don't manage memory, it just works). So a journal a human must open themselves **doesn't deliver its purpose** — same anti-pattern as the rejected `<remember>` tag / the tombstone graveyard (state that exists but the automatic path can't reach). **The user's principle (binding):** *"unless we ship the WHOLE solution in v0.3.2, we don't frame DECISIONS.md as a shipped headline feature — we hold the whole thing until it's recall-complete."* And the recall half can only be VERIFIED live in-chat (a behavioral directive, like W1/E1) — can't be auto-tested, risky to rush against a tag. **DECISION:** v0.3.2 ships with **153 (FTS5 fix) + 152 (validate-index)** as its user-facing scope; the `cmk digest`/DECISIONS.md **CODE stays merged in main** (built, tested, DJ2-idempotency-fixed) but is **un-framed** — pulled from the v0.3.2 CHANGELOG headline + README capability surface + README CLI table (the command stays in the full CLI.md reference; it exists, just isn't a promoted capability). **v0.3.3 (the NEXT version, firm) ships DECISIONS.md complete:** the AI-recall directive (history/evolution/"what did we reject" queries → read `context/DECISIONS.md`; single-decision → fact search — the user's AskUserQuestion pick) + a memory-search skill step + a NEW cut-gate recall stage (DJ4) + the live recall gate. DJ1–DJ3 in the cut-gate become journal-CODE checks, NOT v0.3.2 cut-blockers. _Relates Task 147 (the journal code), Task 156 (the v0.3.3 recall completion — now headline), D-85 (the it-just-works thesis), the DECISIONS.md-recall gap (P-JYH2P5QC), D-17 (document-user-facing-capabilities — applied as DON'T frame an incomplete feature as shipped)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-16) — D-163: automatic recall NEVER reads tombstones; tombstone recovery is a human-only opt-in (v0.3.2 cut-gate finds).** The cut-gate's F-7 probe found `cmk get` on a forgotten id returns `not found` — but the F-7 text + CLI.md `cmk get` description WRONGLY claimed `get` "also reads tombstoned facts (the recovery path)." Reality (verified vs source): `forget` moves the fact to `context/memory/archive/tombstones/<id>.md` AND prunes the DB row; the indexer never walks the tombstone dir; so `get`/`mk_get`/`search`/`mk_search`/the snapshot are all **live-only**. **Settled the product question (was an unsettled gap per memory):** (1) **automatic recall must NEVER read tombstones** — a deleted fact must stay invisible to the agent; an agent confidently recalling a fact you explicitly forgot (e.g. "you use Postgres" after you migrated to SQLite + forgot the old fact) is the worst failure mode of a memory system. (2) The legit "did we try and reject X?" negative-knowledge case belongs in **retract/supersede** (kept + visible — D-161's journal), NOT the tombstone graveyard; using `forget` for it is the wrong-verb signal. (3) **Human recovery is explicit + opt-in only** — `cmk get --include-tombstoned` mirroring the EXISTING `search --include-tombstoned`, optionally `cmk restore <id>`; never automatic. The line: **recovery is a human verb, never an automatic agent behavior.** Distinguishes `forget` (delete → invisible) from `supersede` (evolve → visible). **v0.3.2:** fixed the F-7 + CLI.md docs (get is live-only; the archive file is the recovery artifact). The `--include-tombstoned` FLAG is Task 155 (v0.3.3/v0.4). Facts P-49BQNG9V, P-3BNDZFUW (the stale-MCP-server gotcha found alongside). _Relates D-161 (retract-in-place journal — the OTHER 'forget' that stays visible), Task 110 (forget prunes the row), Task 155 (the recovery flag), the tombstone archive (the durable recovery artifact)._
- **🔍 GAP (2026-06-16) — DECISIONS.md is write-only for AI recall (v0.3.2 cut-gate find → Task 156).** Task 147's decision journal is in ZERO recall directives (injected CLAUDE.md + memory-search skill → only `cmk search`/fact-files/persona) and is NOT indexed by `cmk reindex` (derived view), so `mk_search` never hits it. The journal is great for a HUMAN (chronological trail + PR diff) but invisible to the agent's auto-recall — so its UNIQUE value (decision evolution + retracted/rejected trail) is unreachable, and there's no cut-gate stage testing recall-from-journal (DJ1/2/3 only test the write side). Single-decision recall still works via fact-file search (the fact carries the Why). DESIGN-FIRST task (156, v0.3.3/v0.4): decide whether recall should read DECISIONS.md for decision-HISTORY/"what did we reject" queries (directly or via `cmk digest --decisions`), and if so add a recall directive + a cut-gate recall stage. Surfaced by the user: "when I mention Kamal where do you look, and when would you go to DECISIONS.md?" — answer today: never. Fact P-JYH2P5QC. _Relates Task 147, Task 75 (recall directive/skill), D-161, the tombstone gap D-163 (same class: a surface exists but recall doesn't reach it)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-16) — D-162: Task 141b (node:sqlite migration) REJECTED on perf — better-sqlite3 stays (clean CI data).** The migration's prize was npm-12 immunity (zero native deps); the gate (D-147) was no-measurable-regression on the kit's read/search hot paths. **The dev laptop couldn't resolve it** (measurement noise ±8–22% ≫ the 3% bar — even better-sqlite3-vs-itself swung ±100% on sub-ms ops; the user's "do you get the same results?" exposed this). Built the bench harness (`scripts/bench-storage.mjs`) with batched sampling + self-noise measurement (returns INCONCLUSIVE/exit 2 when its own rsd ≥ the bar — it refuses to report noise as signal) + a `workflow_dispatch` CI job (`bench-storage.yml`, Node 24). **CI gave the clean verdict** (run 27594513495, noise ±0.3–3.7%): **FTS5 keyword query = node:sqlite 1.105× (~10% SLOWER) at ±0.8% noise — a real, trustworthy regression on the kit's MOST COMMON read path**; sqlite-vec KNN = 0.984× (tie); incremental reindex = 1.322× (~32% slower, ±3.7% just over the trust bar but the gap is large). **Per D-147's hardened bar, node:sqlite FAILS** — search latency is paid every query forever; the npm-12 prompt is one-time ("slower is worse than asking the user y/n on script install… we dont sacrifice the kit's purpose" — the user). **Spikes 1 (node:sqlite ships FTS5 on Node 24) + 2 (sqlite-vec loadExtension works, needs `{allowExtension:true}` + the `AND k = N` KNN form) PASSED but are moot** — perf is the gate. **RESOLUTION:** better-sqlite3 STAYS; 141a's install-time `--allow-scripts` ask + HC-8 remain the npm-12 answer. The harness + workflow are KEPT (re-runnable if a future Node release improves node:sqlite's FTS5 perf — that would be the new evidence to re-open this SETTLED line). **v0.3.2 final scope = Tasks 153 + 152 + 147** (153 FTS5 query sanitization, 152 validate-index-completeness, 147 cmk digest + DECISIONS.md), all merged. Saved as fact P-CUV74RDV. _Relates D-147 (the gate this resolves), D-129 (npm-12 / node:sqlite origin), Task 141a (the shipped npm-12 mitigation that stands), ADR-0002 (FTS5 is the keyword layer this protects)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-15) — D-161: Task 147's `context/DECISIONS.md` is an APPEND-ONLY permanent journal, NOT regenerated, NOT parked like MEMORY.md (settled by reasoning with the user before any code).** The user pushed on "how is this different from our DECISION-LOG.md and squad's, and what happens when facts are revised/erased?" — which exposed that my first instinct (regenerate `DECISIONS.md` from live facts, like INDEX.md) was WRONG. **The reasoning:** a decision journal's whole value is the permanent trail — what we decided AND what we moved away from + why. Regenerating from current live facts would silently DROP superseded/forgotten decisions, rewriting history to look like the current state was always obvious — the exact failure CLAUDE.md's decision-trail-preservation rule exists to prevent. **Three models, three jobs:** (1) **MEMORY.md** = bounded hot cache → rolls/parks to dated archives (recent/archive) when it overflows; (2) **INDEX.md** = index of what-currently-exists → regenerated, correctly drops deleted entries; (3) **DECISIONS.md** = permanent ledger → **unbounded, append-only, never parks, never regenerates**. Old decisions are the MOST valuable part of a decision log (they explain why the codebase is shaped as it is), so parking/rolling them would be backwards. **Mechanics:** decision captured → entry appended; superseded → OLD entry annotated in place (struck/marked) + new appended (both stay); forgotten → marked retracted, not deleted. **Squad appends because it has no DB** (its `decisions.md` IS the source of truth — studied live: Title/By/What/Why per entry, `.gitattributes merge=union` to avoid append conflicts, but junk bled in because nothing's structured). The kit appends WITH structure (fact-id links, supersession, no junk) because it has the typed-fact DB underneath. **`cmk digest` stays a SEPARATE regenerated render** (a current-knowledge snapshot — regeneration is correct there, it's "what do we know now" not "what did we decide over time"). **v0.3.2 scope:** only the explicit signals we already have (capture appends; `cmk forget` marks retracted; explicit `superseded_by` annotates); AUTOMATIC semantic contradiction-detection is deferred to F-D / Task 95. **Steal:** `merge=union` on `DECISIONS.md` in `.gitattributes` (we have the Task-154 infra) so teams branching don't conflict. Saved as fact P-3C9V6a76. **SHIPPED 2026-06-15 (v0.3.2):** `decisions-journal.mjs` (pure `updateDecisionsJournal` append-only core + `syncDecisionsJournal` file-IO) + `digest.mjs` + the `cmk digest` verb. Live-verified: capture→append, idempotent re-run, forget→retract-in-place (entry survives + `_(retracted DATE)_`). **Composition bug found+fixed:** forget's `scrubAllScratchpads` walked every `context/*.md` and stripped the journal's `<!-- decision:ID -->` markers — excluded `DECISIONS.md` like `INDEX.md`. **Skill-review caught** a retract-attaches-to-wrong-entry edge (a markerless/hand-edited entry) — bounded the heading search to the entry span. The kit's OWN dogfooded `context/DECISIONS.md` now holds 381 real decision entries (the feature working on itself). _Relates Task 147 (this rewrites its spec), the CLAUDE.md decision-trail-preservation rule, the MEMORY.md rolling-window (design §8) vs this, INDEX.md regeneration (reindex.mjs), squad's decisions.md (studied 2026-06-15, the user's "clone + study" instruction), F-D/Task 95 (deferred auto-supersession), Task 154 (.gitattributes infra)._
- **⚙️ DECISION + FIX (2026-06-15) — D-160: `validate-index-completeness` — the hand-maintained doc catalogs are now structural (Task 152, v0.3.2).** The 2026-06-15 docs review found FOUR stale doc indexes at once (adr/README, research/INDEX, sources/README, process/README) while `validate-references`/`-doc-completeness`/`-doc-registry` all stayed green — those check link-resolution + verb/tool coverage + registry membership, NOT "does each index list every sibling .md." Built `scripts/validate-index-completeness.mjs` (pure `checkIndexCompleteness` + `extractLinkedFiles` + `listSiblingMarkdown` + `CATALOG_INDEXES` config), wired into the `npm test` prerun, mirroring `validate-pack-completeness` (135) + `validate-skill-allowlist` (137.2). **Both directions** (a sibling not listed AND a listed-but-deleted entry both fail); **presence-only** (no content-quality judgment — that's a false-positive magnet); per-index `exclude` allowlist + auto-exclusion of the index file itself. At introduction it caught **5 genuinely-unindexed research notes** (hermes-06-03, dual-surface-06-07, mcp-install-06-08, stellman-06-12, fts5-prep-06-15) — the drift was real, now fixed in research/INDEX.md. **User-scope clarification (the user's load-bearing question):** this polices OUR repo's `docs/` catalogs only — it ships nothing to users (`scripts/` isn't in the npm `files`), and a kit user's `context/memory/INDEX.md` is auto-regenerated by `cmk reindex`/`index-rebuild.mjs`, never hand-edited. Dev-tooling, not a user surface. _Relates Task 135/137.2 (the completeness-validator pattern), D-120 (prose-rule→validator discipline), the CLAUDE.md validators table, the single-source-of-truth ethos applied to derived index views._
- **🐛 BUG + FIX (2026-06-15) — D-159: FTS5 query crash on dots/version strings → per-token auto-quoting (Task 153, v0.3.2).** SURFACED LIVE this session: `mk_search "v0.3 queue remaining tasks ship"` errored `FTS5 parse error — fts5: syntax error near "."`. Root cause: `search.mjs` passed the raw query straight to FTS5 MATCH; FTS5's bareword grammar (letters/digits/underscore/non-ASCII only) rejects `.`, `-`, `:` and the reserved words AND/OR/NOT — so `v0.3` (the `.`) and the kit's own `user-explicit` enum value both crashed. The old `FTS5ParseError` catch only converted the crash to a "wrap in quotes" hint the USER had to act on — invisible-kit failure (D-85). **Fix: `prepareFtsQuery()` — a shared per-token sanitizer** applied before BOTH `MATCH @query` sites (facts + transcripts): tokenize (quoted phrases kept whole), pass safe barewords through (preserving implicit-AND multi-word recall), double-quote any token with special chars or a bare reserved word (escaping embedded `"` SQL-style per the spec). **Research-grounded, not vibes (the user's "want to do research?" + "see what other projects did"):** verified against the **SQLite FTS5 spec §3** (primary source: quoting is the sanctioned escape; `""` is the embedded-quote escape; dot-in-bareword IS a syntax error) AND **basic-memory's real `_prepare_search_term`** (our closest FTS5+markdown analog — confirmed per-token-not-whole-query + the hyphen-needs-quoting class). → [research note](../research/2026-06-15-fts5-query-preparation-cross-system.md). The 3 pre-existing FTS5-error tests (`user-explicit`/`AND`/`badcol:hello`) were INVERTED to assert success — a justified test change (the new behavior is strictly better recall), not a test-to-pass-broken-code edit. Live-verified on the real CLI: `v0.3`, the exact crash string, and `user-explicit` all return cleanly. **Tangent surfaced for Task 141b:** openclaw #62328 ("node:sqlite missing FTS5 module") → added a THIRD gate to the node:sqlite migration spike (confirm FTS5 ships under node:sqlite, or the whole keyword layer breaks). _Relates Task 30 (the FTS5ParseError class this builds on, kept as the final fallback), D-85 (invisible-kit / no-user-action), ADR-0002 (why we're on FTS5 at all — markdown-truth), Task 141b (the new third spike gate)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-15) — D-158: research-note discipline — skip the note when the subject is orthogonal-and-obvious; always report the verdict in chat.** The user 2026-06-15: *"if i bring you a research subject and it has nothing to do with us, I think we can skip writing it down in our research notes."* Adopted with a refinement: ALWAYS assess + give the verdict in chat (proof the subject was actually evaluated), but write a `docs/research/` note ONLY when a future session needs it — a **borrowable idea**, a **settled-line reaffirmation** (where the *why* isn't self-evident), or a **non-obvious rejection**. A subject with zero structural relationship to a memory kit, where the rejection is self-evident, gets chat-only, no permanent file. Rationale: a note's value is audit-trail (so a future session doesn't re-investigate); that value only exists when re-investigation or benefit is plausible. Keeps `docs/research/` signal-dense. **Calibration from this batch:** Qdrant + worker_threads earned notes (non-obvious rejections — server-class-vs-ADR-0015, wrong-tool-vs-our-execution-model — a future session WOULD otherwise re-investigate); agent-infra/sandbox was borderline but earned a short note (a positioning insight + the explicit no-Docker line, D-23-adjacent); a truly orthogonal-and-obvious subject going forward → chat only. Saved as feedback memory `P-HaJCYKSH`. _Relates the adoption-verification sub-rule (negative results are data — but only DURABLE ones earn a file), the single-source-of-truth ethos (don't manufacture state), U-CL7LFRTC (the user verifies/judges relevance)._

- **🔬 REVIEW + ⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-15) — D-156: a full `docs/` review found FOUR hand-maintained index docs drifted behind their contents; fixed + slotted Task 152 to make the class structural.** The user asked for a review of all 106 docs under `docs/`. Approach: structural validators for the mechanical layer (all green — references resolve, every CLI verb + MCP tool documented, no numbering gaps, CLI/MCP parity, registry membership, name-privacy), then read every navigational/index/handoff doc + the user-facing references for CONTENT drift (the frozen history — research/journey/sources/ADR bodies — is point-in-time by design; "review" there = confirm it isn't masquerading as current state, not rewrite it). **Found (commit 5574f2a):** four index docs lagged the files they catalog — `adr/README.md` (missing the ADR-0014 CLI+MCP-unify + ADR-0015 semantic-backend rows; both files Accepted, just unlisted), `process/README.md` (missing `cut-gate.md` — the CURRENT version-agnostic cut guide — + the pdf guide; the "CURRENT" marker sat on the superseded v0.2.0 guide), `research/INDEX.md` (4 unindexed notes: 2026-06-10 simon-v2 + 2026-06-12 ruflo/memclaw/pai), `sources/README.md` (basic-memory + hermes deep-dives unlisted). **All FOUR passed every existing validator** — because `validate-references` checks link RESOLUTION, `validate-doc-completeness` checks verb/tool COVERAGE, `validate-doc-registry` checks registry MEMBERSHIP; NONE checks "does each index list every sibling file." Plus the DECISION that we adopt the field-standard direction.** SURFACED BY the v0.3.1 cold-open (E1, the wedge): a brand-new project inherited the user's TOOLING habits (uv/ruff/types/TDD — all transferred + applied in the scaffold) but NOT his layered-ARCHITECTURE philosophy — it built a plain `routers/` layout, not his `services/repositories/schemas`. **Root cause (verified against BACKUP persona folders — the user: "I'm sure it worked before, did we break something?"):** NOT a code regression. In cut-gate3/cut-gate7 backups the architecture WAS in the active persona (`trust: high`); in cut-gate8/9/10/11 it is NOT. The difference is PHRASING: this session the user stated it as a *philosophy* ("how I build backends: FastAPI is the delivery layer…") not a *universal imperative* ("in EVERY project ALWAYS…"), so `PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE` (auto-persona.mjs:205) correctly graded it `medium` (inferred, not stated-as-rule) → routed to `queues/persona-review.md`. **The actual bug:** the queue's own routing comment promised *"the daily/weekly auto-drain acts on them"* — but `autoDrainQueues` only drained the `review` + `conflict` queues; **the persona-review drain was NEVER implemented.** So medium candidates stranded forever — invisible (surfaced in no doctor/status-line) and unresolvable (no `cmk queue persona`). The cold-open only injects the ACTIVE persona, so the architecture never transferred. **DEEP RESEARCH (the user: "do full research before deciding — clone the real repos, notes are summaries not impl; time + tokens are on our side"):** cloned + read 9 real memory systems (mem0, MemoryOS/MemOS, Letta/MemGPT, langmem, graphiti/Zep, memory-os, claude-mem, basic-memory) + ChatGPT memory + articles → [the persona-promotion research note](../research/2026-06-14-persona-promotion-models-cross-system.md). **Decisive findings: (1) EVERY real system AI-judges promotion automatically; NOT ONE uses a human-gated review queue — we are the sole outlier, and a queue surfaced nowhere with no resolver is the worst version (cost of gating, none of the benefit). (2) Our confidence signal is BACKWARDS: every system that scores durability uses FREQUENCY + RECURRENCE ("persistent = frequently reinforced", heat = visits·recency), NOT imperative phrasing — the architecture philosophy was demonstrated across the WHOLE session (max reinforcement) but graded medium because it wasn't SPOKEN as a rule; every surveyed system would have promoted it.** **DECISION (the user: "adopt the direction + a small v0.3.1 down-payment"):** the field-standard direction — drop the human-review-queue for persona, AI-judge promotion by cross-project recurrence + LLM judgment, post-hoc reversibility (auto-promote then `cmk forget`) instead of pre-gating — is ADOPTED as the target, slotted as **Task 151 (v0.4)**, with this research as its design input. **DOWN-PAYMENT SHIPPED (v0.3.1, this entry):** `resolvePersonaReviewQueue` (auto-persona.mjs) + wired into `autoDrainQueues` — the medium-confidence candidates now auto-promote on the daily/weekly drain (force `confidence:'high'` for the optimistic posture — they already survived a synthesis pass; otherwise the gate that stranded them would re-queue them forever). NO new manual command (the user's binding rule: "automation the AI judges > a user remembering `cmk queue persona`; adding a command is a shitty and wrong fix"). The full recurrence-scored redesign stays Task 151. Tests: `cli-auto-drain.test.js` pins drain→promote→queue-cleared + the no-userDir no-op. _Relates Task 78 (the persona AUTO half / PERSONA_CONFIDENCE_RULE), Task 151 (the v0.4 redesign this researches), the D-6 review-queue auto-drain (the precedent this mirrors), the persona-promotion research note, and the meta-question shared with Task 149/150/148: where the kit relies on a human-gated queue / manual command, AI-judged automation belongs instead._
- **🐞 BUG+FIX (2026-06-14) — D-153: the recall skill RE-DERIVED structure/architecture from code instead of recalling it — the trigger had a self-contradicting skip-clause (cut-gate v0.3.1 live-test, Session 2, the user: "this looks like something broke, it used to work").** The v0.3.0 recall ladder (the headline) worked on *"what did we decide about X"* phrasings but FAILED on structure/location questions. **4-run live sample, phrasing-DETERMINISTIC (not session variance):** *"what did we decide about structure"* → skill fired, memory-led ✅; *"what are my standing rules"* → answered from the injected snapshot ✅; BUT *"how is this project structured"* → `Glob **/*` + `Read app/main.py` (code crawl) ✗; *"where does the business logic live"* → `Glob app/**/*.py` + `Read` 3 files (code crawl) ✗. **Root cause (verified by reading all 3 mechanisms in the scaffolded skill):** the `memory-search` skill's `description` said *"Skip when the question is purely about current code state (use Read/Grep)"* — and a structure/location question ("where does X live", "how is this built") pattern-matches MORE strongly to "current code state" than to the past-tense "what did we decide" trigger examples, so **the skill instructed ITSELF not to fire on exactly the questions whose answer is a recorded decision in the deep archive** (the structure facts live in `context/memory/project_*.md`, NOT in the injected snapshot — confirmed 0 structure mentions in MEMORY.md — so the model MUST search to answer from memory, and the skip-clause told it not to). The CLAUDE.md preamble actually covered it ("what's our X / what's the setup → query memory"), but the skill description's skip-clause OVERRODE that. **FIX (one concern, 3 aligned surfaces so they reinforce not contradict):** (a) the skill `description` now names structure/architecture/layout/"where does X live" as recall triggers AND narrows the skip-clause to genuinely-live code ("uncommitted / in-progress / a file you just edited this turn"), explicitly calling "where does X live" a RECORDED-decision question; (b) the per-prompt hint (`capture-prompt.mjs`) adds "project structure/architecture, where things live — recall it, don't re-read the code"; (c) the CLAUDE.md recall preamble adds "how is this project structured/built / where does X live / what's the architecture" to the query-memory list. Plugin mirror synced (byte-identical validator). Regression tests pin the structure triggers + the narrowed skip-clause in `cli-skill-scaffold.test.js` + the hint in `cli-capture-prompt.test.js`. **PRIMARY-SOURCE CATCH (the user: "do you want to check the docs for skills?" + the maintainer's personal skill-authoring articles — the "did you check the primary source?" rule):** the first draft of the widened description was **1340 chars — OVER Anthropic's hard 1024-char `description` limit**, which per the Agent-Skills docs means the skill **SILENTLY fails to load** (no error) — the fix would have DISABLED recall worse than the bug it fixed, surfacing only as a mysterious live-test failure. The docs also flagged two second-person `you` (the "always third-person" rule — the description is injected into the system prompt). Both fixed: rewrote to **1021 chars, third-person**, triggers + narrowed skip intact. Added STRUCTURAL guards (1024-char + third-person + no-XML-brackets assertions on BOTH scaffolded skills in `cli-skill-scaffold.test.js`) so the silent-non-load class can never recur — the project's prose-rule→validator discipline. The docs ALSO confirmed the fix's approach: their troubleshooting table prescribes exactly "never triggers → add trigger phrases" + "triggers constantly → add Do-NOT-use conditions" (my fix does both), and names our exact bug class — "the most common regression is a description edit that narrows triggers too aggressively." I reasoned WHAT correctly from feel but would have gotten the format CONTRACT (length/person) wrong without the primary source. _Sources: platform.claude.com Agent-Skills best-practices + overview; a personal-wiki "Complete Guide to Claude Skills Building" clipping._ **Shipped IN v0.3.1** (the user: "we need to fix it now") — the recall ladder is the kit's headline; cutting it with recall broken on "how is this built" was not acceptable. NOTE: this is a v0.3.0-introduced gap (the skill shipped then), surfaced only by the cut-gate's real Session-2 recall test — unit tests can't see model-trigger behavior (the live-test-every-task rule earning its keep again). _Relates Task 75 (the recall ladder / D-105 lane), the W1/D3 cut-gate gates, the live-test-every-task rule, the "did the skill FIRE" gate vs the "was recall CORRECT" gate (D1 passed all 4 runs — the user always got the right answer; the failure was HOW, re-deriving from code, which D3 gates against)._ **LIVE RE-TEST VERDICT (2026-06-14, after re-pack + re-install of the fixed 0.3.1 into cut-gate11): FIX CONFIRMED ENOUGH.** Both previously-failing prompts now PASS: *"how is this project structured"* → "Let me check memory first before re-reading the code" → memory-search skill fires → `cmk search`, ZERO code crawl ✅; *"where does the business logic live, and why"* → skill fires → `cmk search` + `cmk get`, answers from recorded facts (incl. the high-trust philosophy fact) with ZERO code crawl ✅. All 4 phrasings now recall correctly. **So the user's "if not enough, clone the real repos and research" path is NOT triggered for v0.3.1** — the cross-project recall-architecture study (judgment-pulled vs always-search vs inject-everything, via CLONING the real repos since notes are summaries not impl — the user's point) is logged as a v0.4 recall-lane input, not a blocker. **Process hazard noted:** the re-install was blocked by 6 orphaned `cmk mcp serve` node processes (from prior cut-gate11 CC sessions) holding `better_sqlite3.node` (EBUSY) — the MCP servers accumulate and lock the binding against `npm install -g` on Windows; killed them to unblock. Worth a v0.x note (graceful mcp-serve shutdown / install-time lock detection). **FIX v2 — GENERALITY (the user pushed, correctly: "is it general enough? if I ask something esoteric or roundabout, not precise like we did, will it search?" + "ride on the shoulders of the great… why trial-and-error? do the research now").** v1 fixed the SPECIFIC prompts by adding structure PHRASINGS — but that's brittle: a phrase-list only catches listed phrasings, and an oblique/roundabout question ("why is everything so spread out?") matches none. Did the research properly this time (not trial-and-error): (1) **Anthropic Agent-Skills docs + the OFFICIAL `skill-creator` skill (local, the gold standard) + real production description fields** (frontend-design, claude-md-improver, build-mcp-server) — finding: triggering is **SEMANTIC INTENT MATCHING, not keyword matching**; the description should LEAD with a general intent class, examples illustrative-not-exhaustive (Anthropic's own descriptions do exactly this); skill-creator literally lists "optimize a skill's description for better triggering accuracy" as a task. (2) **Cloned + read 9 real memory repos** (claude-mem, **memsearch** — our direct inspiration, mempalace, mem0, claude-remember, claude_memory, basic-memory, memory-os, graphiti) for how they trigger recall. **Decisive finding: our judgment-pulled-skill architecture is RIGHT (it's memsearch's exact model) but we shipped only its HARD HALF.** Almost no real system relies on judgment-from-description alone — they backstop it (5/9 inject-at-session-start, 2/9 always-search, others a per-turn nudge or a user command). **memsearch's key move we were missing: its skill description says "Also fire when you see a `[memsearch] Memory available` hint" — linking its per-turn UserPromptSubmit nudge TO the skill.** We already HAD the nudge (capture-prompt.mjs) but our description never referenced it — two disconnected mechanisms. memory-os's cautionary lesson: even always-injecting didn't make the model USE memory (it re-discovered injected facts) — so always-search is not a magic fix, it trades a trigger problem for a cost+usage problem; DON'T switch to it. **v2 fix (evidence-based):** rewrote the description to (a) LEAD with the general intent principle ("Fire whenever the answer might be something the project already established, HOWEVER the question is phrased"), (b) mark examples "illustrative, not a checklist" + add an OBLIQUE example ("why is everything so spread out?"), (c) **reference the hint** ("Also fire when a `[claude-memory-kit] Memory available` hint appears") — memsearch's move, closing the loop with our existing nudge. 999 chars, third-person. Tests rewritten to pin the GENERALITY (the "however phrased" generalizer + "illustrative" + hint-reference + oblique example), not specific phrasings. _v2 sources: Anthropic skill-creator (local plugin cache) + Agent-Skills docs; the 9-repo clone study (the user's "go to the projects we researched" + "clone them, notes are summaries not impl"). Relates Task 149 (the v0.4 always-search-vs-judgment-pulled ADR — now informed by this code study), Task 75 (recall ladder), U-6N9S9XZS (the user always reads relevant projects)._
- **🐞 ISSUE+FIX (2026-06-14) — D-152: a committed `INDEX.md` can LAG behind its fact files after an auto-extract session — root cause was a SILENTLY SWALLOWED reindex failure; fixed to be observable (surfaced by the user during the cut-gate: "why would you need to reindex INDEX? sounds like a problem" → "fix").** During this session the Stop-hook auto-extract wrote 5 fact files (07:09–07:10) that were durably on disk but ABSENT from the working-tree `context/memory/INDEX.md` until a manual `cmk reindex` added them (verified: 0 in the pre-commit INDEX, 5 after; HC-4 then PASS at 151 facts). **Root cause:** `writeFact` rebuilds INDEX.md best-effort with a SWALLOWED catch (write-fact.mjs:264-268 — "the fact is on disk; next reindex/search self-heals"); under the live session's hook concurrency (detached Stop-hook child, possible index-DB contention, or the child hitting the hook ceiling before the rebuild lands) the in-child INDEX rebuild didn't make it into the committed file. **Why it's NOT data loss:** the fact FILES are the source of truth; INDEX.md is a derived human-readable view. **Why it's still a real wrinkle (not fully "self-healing" as the code comment claims):** `cmk search` rebuilds the SQLite index DB (`reindexBoot`) before reading — but INDEX.md is a SEPARATE markdown artifact that search does NOT rewrite, so a lagging INDEX.md does NOT self-heal on search; it stays stale until the next `writeFact` create or an explicit `cmk reindex`. And because INDEX.md is COMMITTED to git, a stale derived view can be committed + travel to clones/teammates. **Options considered:** (a) make the reindex failure OBSERVABLE instead of silently swallowed; (b) gitignore INDEX.md — REJECTED by the user ("why the hell would you gitignore index????") and correctly so: INDEX.md is the committed, human-readable, travels-with-clone memory index, a FEATURE of the git-native design (a teammate/swarm agent gets the readable index without running anything) — NOT a disposable cache like the binary SQLite DB; conflating the two was my error; (c) add a pre-commit / doctor HC — HC-4 ALREADY detects the drift (fact-file set vs INDEX-referenced set) and emits `recoveryCommand: cmk reindex`; (d) accept the lag. **FIX SHIPPED (option a + the existing c):** the real defect was that the rebuild failure was SILENT — a detached child's reindex killed mid-rebuild left INDEX lagging with ZERO trace, undiagnosable. write-fact.mjs now records an `INDEX_REBUILD_FAILED` audit entry on a thrown reindex (Door 4 — observability; the fact still lands, best-effort preserved); HC-4 still surfaces the drift to the user with `cmk reindex` as the correction. Investigated the alternative theories first and ruled them out: NOT a single-process race (writeFact is sync; 8 concurrent in-process writes all land), NOT a multi-process race (8 separate concurrent OS processes all land — the last writer reads every file), NOT a v0.3.0-vs-current divergence (the published binary has byte-identical reindex code). The cause is the swallowed transient. A test-only `_reindexFn` seam drives the failure path; regression test pins Doors 1 (write still succeeds) + 2 (fact on disk) + 4 (audit entry present, and absent on the happy path — no false alarms). NOT a lock subsystem (over-engineering — the wholesale rebuild is self-correcting whenever it actually RUNS; the gap was only the silent failure). **CLARIFICATION (2026-06-14, the user's challenge: "users will not run cmk reindex to fix a problem we have in our kit… i hope this is not how you fixed it" + "are we sure we have a problem and not a false positive?"):** the framing above OVERSTATED this as a "bug." Re-examined, it is a **known by-design best-effort behavior, working as specified** — NOT a regression, NOT a new defect. Three corrections to the record: (1) **RECALL is never affected** — `cmk search` reads the SQLite DB, which `reindexBoot` auto-rebuilds incrementally on EVERY query (subcommands.mjs:400, no user command); PROVEN on the real 0.3.1 artifact by deleting a fact's line from INDEX.md and confirming `cmk search` still returns it from the DB. INDEX.md is a human-readable POINTER doc, explicitly NOT loaded at session start (inject-context.mjs:140) and NOT read by search — so a lagging INDEX.md is cosmetic, never a wrong/missing search result. (2) **The self-heal is automatic, not the manual `cmk reindex` I implied** — `reindex()` rebuilds INDEX.md WHOLESALE from every fact file (not append), so the NEXT successful `writeFact` fully heals any prior drift with no command. This was incidental (untested); now PINNED as a contract by `cli-write-fact-reindex-failure.test.js`'s "a later successful write fully rebuilds a drifted INDEX" test. (3) **HC-4 + the #181 audit entry remain the diagnosable safety net** for the residual "lagged AND no later capture AND a human reads INDEX.md by hand" window. **DECISION: ship as-is; the SessionStart auto-heal was considered and REJECTED as over-engineering** (per-session-start fact-dir I/O on the protected hot path to fix a cosmetic lag in a convenience file that already self-heals on next write). The genuinely-real bugs this cut-gate found were the `<private>` leaks (D-148/D-151) — those ARE fixed; this INDEX item was a known tradeoff I mislabeled. _Relates Task 85/110 (the writer-owns-INDEX + lazy-reindex design), D-114 (#154 forget/INDEX fix), HC-4/HC-5, the lazy-framing rule (a silently-swallowed catch IS a silent "expected fail"), the live-test-every-task rule (this only shows under real hook concurrency, never in unit tests), the over-engineering anti-pattern (the rejected SessionStart auto-heal)._
- **🐞 BUG+FIX (2026-06-14) — D-151: `<private>` secret leaked into the fact TITLE via the 80-char title slice (cut-gate v0.3.1 clean-build re-run finding).** The clean-build cut-gate (re-install from merged main + real `cmk remember` against real input — the live-test-every-task rule) caught a leak the #179 unit tests structurally couldn't: `rememberRich` derives the fact title as `text.split('\n')[0].slice(0, 80)` BEFORE the privacy strip. When the 80-char cut lands INSIDE a `<private>…</private>` span it severs the closing tag (`</private>` → `</priv`), so `writeFact`'s `<private>[\s\S]*?</private>` regex — which the #179 fix relies on — no longer matches the broken span, and the secret survives in the frontmatter `title:` + INDEX.md (the body was correctly redacted; only the truncated title leaked). **The composition class** (separately-correct-jointly-broken): the 80-char title truncation (remember-core, correct in isolation) composed badly with the privacy strip (write-fact, correct in isolation) — truncation can sever a tag the regex needs intact. The #179 unit tests passed *intact* tags straight to `writeFact`, never exercising the truncation path; only the real CLI `rememberRich` path (title-derived-then-sliced) hits it. **Fix:** strip `<private>` in `remember-core` (`rememberRich` + `richFactTitle`) BEFORE deriving/slicing the title, so the slice only ever sees redacted text; `body`/`slug`/`sourceSha1` already derive from the now-redacted `headline`. writeFact's strip stays as the backstop. Regression test added to `cli-private-tag-write-path.test.js` with a fixture-guard asserting the secret survives the cut while the closing tag is severed (so the test can't silently stop exercising the bug). Verified on a fresh clean-build sandbox: title = `[private content redacted]`, secret absent from disk, even the filename clean. _Relates D-148 (the original #179 write-boundary fix), the composition-verification rule, the live-test-every-task rule (unit-green ≠ works-on-real-input — that lesson again)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-14) — D-150: privacy becomes AUTO-JUDGED, not user-tagged — Claude judges sensitivity at extraction time the same way it judges save-worthiness; default action = DROP from the committed tier (Option A).** The user's framing (binding): *"i dont understand why a user needs to wrap a sentence with `<private>` to make it private… it's like if the user wanted you to remember something he'd have to wrap it with `<remember>`."* This is the kit's OWN auto-extract thesis applied consistently to privacy: we already auto-decide what to KEEP (auto-extract) and auto-catch the highest-risk SECRETS (Poison_Guard); the `<private>` tag was the one spot we punted judgment back to the user — and it's the WORST spot for a prospective tag, because you don't know a passage is sensitive until you've already typed it (by then it's in the transcript). **The model:** at extraction time, if a candidate fact contains personal/sensitive content (health detail, real name, home address, private grievance — beyond Poison_Guard's credential regexes), Claude does NOT write it to the git-committed project tier. **Default = Option A (the user's pick): drop from the committed tier**; genuinely-useful-but-sensitive content falls through to `context.local/` (gitignored, this-machine-only) rather than vanishing — mirrors Poison_Guard's refuse-to-commit-and-don't-make-the-user-tag model, keeps one uniform mental model ("the kit refuses to commit risky things; you never tag"). Rejected: B (keep+`private:true` — still WRITES the text to the committed tier, protects only at the inject/search layer) and C (ask-before-write — reintroduces the friction auto-extract exists to remove). **The `<private>` tag SURVIVES as the explicit override** — the rare "scrub THIS passage" escape hatch, exactly parallel to how `cmk remember` is the explicit override on top of auto-extract; documented as override, NOT the primary path. **Lane: a NEW task in the v0.3.x within-paradigm queue** (auto-sensitivity judgment fits the polish lane — make the kit better without changing what it is, D-130). PR #179 stays focused (SHA-256 fix + the existing tag-strip-at-write-boundary from the cut-gate finding) so v0.3.1 cuts on schedule; the auto-judgment task ships after. NOT folded into #179 (one-focused-change-per-PR); NOT deferred to v0.4.0 (would ship v0.3.1 with the known-weak privacy UX un-addressed for a whole minor cycle). _Relates D-149 (the PR #179 it rode in on), design §6.6/§6.7 (privacy-tag + Poison_Guard), the auto-extract thesis (design §6.0), D-130 (the lane)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-14) — D-149: the kit's content-fingerprint convention migrated SHA-1 → SHA-256 kit-wide.** PR #179's CodeQL FAILURE was NOT a transient (the assistant's "known transient quick-exit" label was a lazy-framing MISTAKE the user caught — there is no such transient for this alert): it was a genuine high-severity `js/weak-cryptographic-algorithm` at memory-write.mjs, surfaced because the privacy-strip made taint-tracking see `<private>`-derived text flow into a `createHash('sha1')` content-fingerprint. The digests are NON-cryptographic (dedup + change-detection + provenance), so SHA-1 was never a security flaw here — but a weak-hash sink on every fingerprint site is noise that hides real findings, AND eight modules each rolled their own `createHash('sha1')` (drift surface). **The fix (the user's call: migrate the WHOLE convention, not suppress):** a single `content-hash.mjs` → `hashContent()` (SHA-256) helper; all 8 sites routed through it (memory-write, auto-extract, remember-core, conflict-queue, import-anthropic-memory, import-claude-md, index-rebuild `sha1OfContent`, transcript-index `sha1`); the `// NOSONAR` markers removed. **On-disk FIELD names kept for back-compat** (`source_sha1` frontmatter key, `files.sha1` checkpoint column) — only the ALGORITHM changed; renaming the YAML key / db column would break existing fact files + checkpoints. **Upgrade behavior:** the `files`-table mtime+sha1 diff key now computes a 64-char SHA-256; every existing checkpoint mismatches ONCE on the first post-upgrade boot and self-heals via the normal reindex (the same digest-changed → reindex mechanic that handles any edit). The two existing SHA-256 sites (mcp-server composite key, semantic-backend embedding-cache key) left as-is (no alert, different contracts). _Relates D-148 (the cut-gate that surfaced the privacy fix), the lazy-framing rule (the "transient" mislabel), design §9.2 + the §frontmatter source_sha1 table row (both updated to SHA-256)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-13) — D-147: node:sqlite migration (141b) is GATED on NO MEASURABLE REGRESSION on the read/search paths — the user's hardened bar.** "Easier on the npm-12 problem" must not buy "slower search," and the user hardened the bar from my proposed ≤10-15% to **no measurable regression**: *"slower is worse than asking the user y/n on script install — the ux is not optimal but we dont sacrifice the kit's purpose."* The principle (durable): the npm-12 prompt is a ONE-TIME setup cost; search latency is paid on EVERY query forever — never trade a permanent recurring tax to remove a one-time annoyance. The kit's purpose is fast reliable recall; that's the wow, and it's not negotiable for install elegance. **Operational definition of "no measurable regression"** (so it can't later be fudged into "4% is basically noise"): `scripts/bench-storage.mjs` (built at 141b) times BOTH backends on the kit's real hot paths — FTS5 keyword query, sqlite-vec cosine query, per-read incremental reindex (the every-search cost since Task 110) [these three are the GATED read/search paths] + reindexFull bulk insert + single `cmk remember` write [reported, looser]. Each op run N≥20× warm, same machine/corpus (recall-bench fixture or dogfood-sized index), interleaved A/B to cancel drift. **PASS = node:sqlite p95 on each gated read path is within the measurement noise band of better-sqlite3** — concretely, `node:sqlite_p95 ≤ better_p95 × 1.03` (3% = noise floor for this harness, NOT a perf budget; if node:sqlite is genuinely faster or equal it sails, and a real >3% slowdown on any read path FAILS). Write/bulk paths reported but not gated (off the interactive path). **If it fails: 141b does NOT ship — better-sqlite3 stays, 141a's install-time ask remains the npm-12 answer.** The cross-platform sqlite-vec `loadExtension` spike is the OTHER gate (D-129); both must pass. _Relates D-109 (bake-off precedent), D-129/D-146, 141a (the bridge that stands if 141b fails)._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-13) — D-146: version sequencing — v0.3.1 (this batch, live-tested first) → v0.3.2 (node:sqlite + v0.3.x lane close) → v0.4.0 (Kiro, UNCHANGED).** The user flagged my v0.4.0-minor suggestion as clobbering a reserved lane — correct. **The kit versions by LANE-THEME, not strict semver** (an existing convention I failed to check first): the MINOR digit tracks the differentiator/lane, the PATCH digit tracks shipments within a lane. **v0.3.x = the within-paradigm POLISH lane** (D-130 — make the kit better without changing what it is); its differentiator (recall) already shipped at v0.3.0, so the 10 additive-feature PRs of this sweep (config/import/near-dup/status-line/health/secrets/validators) are PATCH-level under the one-differentiator-per-minor rule — NOT a v0.4 minor. **v0.4.0 is RESERVED for the Kiro cross-agent BREADTH headline (D-127, the user's daily-IDE dogfood) — labeling this batch v0.4.0 would have squatted on it + silently shoved Kiro to v0.5.** Sequencing: v0.3.1 cut after the cut-gate live-test passes; v0.3.2 = node:sqlite (D-147) + the Node-floor bump + 96/130 if ready; v0.4.0 = Kiro untouched. _Relates D-127 (v0.4 = Kiro), D-130 (the v0.3.x lane), the one-differentiator-per-minor rule, RELEASE-PLAN._
- **🔬 CUT-GATE FINDINGS (2026-06-14) — D-148: the v0.3.1 cut-gate live-test found TWO real bugs that 1857+ green tests missed — the live-test-every-task rule earning its keep before the tag.** The user gated v0.3.1 on a manual cut-gate before publishing; the CLI feature sweep + the user's "check the files created" directive surfaced two pre-existing-but-real bugs:
  - **BUG #1 — `cmk repair --index`/`--all` threw since Task 49 (FIXED, PR #178 merged `9aad241`).** `repairIndex` called the production `reindexFull({projectRoot,userDir})` with NO `db`, but `reindexFull` calls `db.exec` → "Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'exec')". Masked ~3 weeks because every repair test injected a reindexer MOCK (the seam-injection blind spot — same class as Task 143/129 this session). Fix: repairIndex opens its own db (openIndexDb), passes it, closes in finally; injected-reindexer test path stays db-less. Class-closed: the only other reindexFull callers (cmk reindex --full, bench-recall) already passed db. New test exercises the REAL no-mock path. cut-gate.md F-11 updated to probe repair --index on the real path.
  - **BUG #2 — `<private>` leaked to committed files via the CLI write path (FIXED, PR #179).** `<private>…</private>` was honored ONLY by the UserPromptSubmit hook (capture-prompt.mjs), so `cmk remember "...<private>SECRET</private>..."` / `mk_remember` / import wrote the secret VERBATIM into committed MEMORY.md + fact files. The design.md claim that write-fact already stripped it was STALE/false. The user's directive — *"you also need to check the files created"* — is what caught it ON DISK. Fix: `sanitizePrivacyTags` runs FIRST in BOTH shared write boundaries (memoryWrite + writeFact), all tiers, before home-path-sanitize/Poison_Guard/id-gen. Whole-surface covered (skill-review audit + live-proven): cmk remember/mk_remember→memoryWrite; rich/import/graduation/merge-facts→writeFact (compose it); the conflict-queue direct-write bypass is COVERED because the strip runs before detectConflicts (live-proven: a `<private>` near-dup → conflicts.md → 0 secret). Strip-before-Poison_Guard is intentional (a user-marked-private secret becomes [redacted] before screening, so it's not logged to poison-guard.log — logging redacted-private content would itself leak). design.md §"re-apply privacy" comment corrected. **THE META-LESSON:** both bugs were INVISIBLE to the full green suite because tests MOCKED the real boundary (repair's reindexer; the hook-vs-write-boundary split for privacy) — the live-test against real input + real files is structurally the only thing that catches the mock-hides-the-contract class. **NEXT (the user's directive, recorded P-ZMCV7XLP):** after #179 merges, RE-INSTALL the kit fresh from merged main + RE-RUN the full CLI cut-gate against that clean build (not the dev tree), verifying created files are clean, THEN the user cuts v0.3.1. _Relates D-146 (v0.3.1 lane), the live-test-every-task rule, the seam-injection blind-spot class (Task 143/129), P-SKH3KKJS (both fixed via branch+PR, not direct-to-main)._

- **📋 NOTE (2026-06-12) — D-136: npm-v12 community-discussion follow-up (the user's link) — one maintainer CORRECTION + one doc addition; the 141a mitigation stands unchanged.** From github.com/orgs/community/discussions/198547 (npm maintainer JamieMagee): (1) **v12's default is SOFT mode** — unapproved scripts skip WITH A WARNING and the install SUCCEEDS; hard failure only under explicit `strict-allow-scripts=true`. This refines D-129's framing and STRENGTHENS the 141a design: the breakage is a warning scrolling past in `-g` output, then a crash at first use — exactly the silent state the install-time probe + ask exists to catch. - **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-126: H1 (the clone) caught a SyntaxError LIVE ON MAIN + CRLF-blind memory reads — Task 139, gate-day bugs #7 + #8.** (1) The Task-138 merge-emitter edit shipped a literal line terminator inside a string (the heredoc-mangling class, third strike of the day): real Node refuses it; **three masks aligned green** — vitest/esbuild parsed leniently, CI's install+doctor smoke never lazy-imports conflict-queue, and the implementer's grep-filtered test output hid the suite-level crash (44 "passed" = the OTHER two files; the crashed suite's tests simply weren't counted). `cmk search` died instantly in the clone. Fix: one char + **`validate-node-parse.mjs`** (every src module must import under real Node in the npm-test prerun) — the engine-divergence class is now structurally closed. (2) **CRLF blindness:** default Windows git (`autocrlf=true`) rewrites committed memory files at clone; the strict-LF frontmatter boundary and `split('
')` readers left `
` on every line — the clone indexed 0 of 18 facts. The kit's PORTABILITY promise (H1, "another computer") was broken on the most common Windows config. Fix: tolerant reads (`/
?
/` + `
?` boundary), writes re-join LF (self-healing); `.gitattributes` prevention parked as follow-up. **Meta:** the implementer's own tooling discipline (heredocs for code edits) caused #7 — heredocs are now banned for code edits in favor of the Edit tool (the lesson fired three times before sticking). _Relates D-125, Task 137 (the gate-vs-automation program), CLAUDE.md tooling traps._
- **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-125: imported bullets broke the next reindex — Task 138 (cut-gate9 F-13, gate-day bug #5).** The F-sweep's seeded real-input import applied cleanly, then `cmk search` reported "index refresh failed: NOT NULL constraint failed: observations.write_source" (graceful stale-index degradation — the message worked). Root cause: `import-anthropic-memory` hand-rolled its provenance comment (`write_source:` key) instead of using the shared `writeBullet` builder; the reindex parser only reads the canonical `write:` key. The shared-modules rule (CLAUDE.md) violated at write time surfaced as a composition failure at read time — the EXACT drift class the rule exists to prevent, and the import suite (Task 114) missed it because no test composed import with reindex. Fix: `writeBullet` + enum `write: imported` + real sha1; composition pin (import → reindexFull → searchable); 2 old tests pinned the broken shape, updated. **The review's emitter sweep found the SAME class in `mergeScratchpadBullets`** (conflict-queue merge-both wrote a `write:`-less comment into the scratchpad → first reindex after any merge resolution would fail identically) — fixed in the same PR via the same shared builder (+ `merged` joins the write-source enum; the merged_from trail lives in the audit entry). **Gate-day total: FIVE code bugs + one guide bug** — D-122/123/124/125 + C3 + (the F-13 class feeds Task 137.4's composition checks). _Relates Task 38a/114, CLAUDE.md "Shared modules", D-124._
- **🐛 BUG/FIX (2026-06-11) — D-124: the output cap wrote a CORRUPTED memory — Task 136 (cut-gate9 Session 2).** The user's recall probe surfaced P-BaTM3L42 with body "The `clau" (9 chars): a dense Session-1 turn emitted 3 rich facts (>2000 bytes), `compressor.mjs` defensively slices at `maxOutputBytes`, and `parseRichFacts` accepted the clipped trailing block — the parser had no concept of a truncated fact. The model worked around it live (read the file, inferred from the title) — the ladder degraded gracefully — but a corrupted fact on disk violates the never-lose-context promise's quality half. **Fix:** an EOF-unterminated BEGIN_FACT block (the slice's unique signature — well-formed output always closes) is dropped + counted (`clipped_facts_dropped` in extract.log); the extraction budget raised 2000→8192 (3-4 rich facts ≈ 2.5-4KB legitimate). Losing the clipped fact beats storing a mangled one. **Today's gate total: FOUR bugs** (D-122 dedup self-poisoning, D-123 skill allowlist, the C3 guide probe, D-124 clipped facts) — the manual gate keeps out-finding 1700+ green tests. _Relates Task 103 (rich facts), design §6.4, D-122._

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-118: Task 104.2 + 104.3 shipped (PR #158, merged `1541efa`) — TASK 104 COMPLETE; the recall waterfall has its floor (the L3 raw tier is searchable).** Build: `transcript_chunks` + FTS + `vec_transcripts` (the embedding cache is SHARED — content-addressed, the same text embeds once regardless of scope); the chunker (`## ` turns → ≤1500-char windows, every window keeps its heading); sync rides `reindexBoot`/`reindexFull` via per-file sha1 checkpoints in the shared `files` table (`transcript:` key prefix). **Two composition hazards caught before they shipped:** (1) reindexBoot's orphan-prune would have eaten the `transcript:` checkpoints every boot (they're not observation sources) — the prune now skips the prefix and the transcript sync prunes its own orphans; (2) a flaky test exposed a REAL mtime-resolution race (two appends within the filesystem's mtime granularity made the second invisible — rapid Stop hooks are the production shape) — the mtime fast-path was dropped, sha1 is the authority. **Search surface:** `search()` scope param ('facts' default | 'transcripts'); fact-only filters (tier/minTrust/since) are REJECTED under the transcripts scope (honest, not silent); hits carry synthetic `T:<file>:<line>` ids (chunks are locations, not facts — no [PUL] identity, no trust; the id keys hybrid RRF fusion and is the drill-back handle); `cmk search --scope transcripts` + `mk_search {scope}` parity; the memory-search skill gains Step 4 (LAST RESORT, with the capture-back nudge: "if something found here is durably useful, say so"). **104.3 retention settled in design §19.4.1:** full history, growth bounded at the source (the 104.1 caps), knob deferred with the repo-size trigger. _Relates D-117 (104.1), Task 65 (the semantic machinery generalized), Task 75.1 (the skill), §19, D-70/D-72._
- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-117: Task 104 sub-structured (2 PRs, the Task-108 precedent) + 104.1 shipped (PR #157) — the kit's transcript now records TOOL ACTIVITY (the L3 raw tier's capture half).** **The ordering insight: capture is time-sensitive, search is not** — every turn that passes uncaptured is unbackfillable, while the index can be built over the accumulated record any time; so 104.1 (enriched capture) ships first, 104.2 (the `--scope transcripts` L3 search) next. **Sub-decisions settled:** (a) detail = +tool calls/results (compact, capped: 300-char result snippets, 4000-char block, honest "…N more truncated" overflow), NOT thinking (bulky, rarely recall-worthy, privacy-heavier); (b) the L3 index = a SEPARATE scope, never mixed into L1 results (the MemPalace last-resort contract); (c) retention = full history (the differentiator vs native's ~30-day machine-local expiry; growth bounded by the per-turn caps; a retention knob deferred, trigger = transcripts dominating repo size). **Build:** new pure [`turn-tools.mjs`](../../packages/cli/src/turn-tools.mjs) (`extractTurnToolActivity` + bounded `readTranscriptTail`, 768KB tail) reads the current turn from the Stop payload's `transcript_path` (Anthropic's live JSONL — extracting the turn at capture time is NOT the JSONL-copy crutch the user rejected 2026-06-06); capture-turn appends a privacy-sanitized `**Tools:**` block under the assistant entry; now.md + the auto-extract turn-file stay TEXT-ONLY (tool noise must not feed the compressor/extractor). **The format is not a documented contract — the user's push ("there are several projects you can examine and the docs") drove a 6-session/4-project empirical survey that caught two variants a single sample missed:** `message.content` can be a plain STRING (not only a block list) and `tool_result.content` comes as STRING or LIST; the parser handles both + degrades to null on anything else (a format shift can degrade the enrichment, never the capture). **Live-tested on the most real input available: this session's own 7.8MB JSONL** — the bin extracted the session's actual tool calls (PR merges, doc edits) into a capped, readable block. _Relates Task 104/65/75, §19 (the L3 floor), D-70/D-72 (the waterfall), the 2026-06-06 user directive._

- **⚙️ DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-111: Task 46 shipped (PR #152, merged `f2bbf0d`) — semantic recall is "dependency opt-in, behavior default-on" (the user’s default-on push, resolved).** _Live-tested end-to-end on the real bin + real npm registry + real embedder (sandboxed user tier): real `npm install -g` → settings flip → warm (1s, cached) → bare `cmk search` ran hybrid via the configured default and ranked both paraphrase probes #1; fallback / exit-2 / pin paths verified. `mk_search`-in-a-live-session stays flagged for the manual v0.3.0-cut session. So: `cmk install --with-semantic` = npm-installs the embedder globally + writes `search.default_mode: hybrid` (only after npm succeeds — no half-state) + pre-warms the model (the one-time download happens at INSTALL, not as a surprise on first search); from then on bare `cmk search` and `mk_search` run hybrid with no flags. `--no-semantic` pins keyword; bare install prints a one-line tip. **Degradation contract:** configured-default-unavailable → graceful keyword fallback + stderr note (a default must never break every search); explicit `--mode=semantic` unavailable → exit 2 + install hint (you asked, you get the truth). **Composition fix found by TDD:** the default-mode resolution initially rode the same dynamic import as the heavy prepare → suspended the KEYWORD path’s synchronous contract (caught by cli-subcommands-dispatch); fixed by statically importing the light resolver (module top-level = node builtins; the embedder stays lazy). Tasks.md 46 reshaped post-ADR-0015 with the original spec preserved. _Relates Task 65/ADR-0015, D-105, the user’s 2026-06-10 default-on question._
- **🏁 DECISION (2026-06-10) — D-109: Task 65 shipped (PR #150) — the Layer-5b semantic backend is REAL and the §9.3.1 deferral is RESOLVED ([ADR-0015](../adr/0015-semantic-backend-sqlite-vec-plus-local-onnx-embedder.md)). Wow #2 (recall with reasoning) = video parity.** Decision: **sqlite-vec (v0.1.9, ~300KB regular dep) inside the kit’s EXISTING SQLite index + `Xenova/bge-base-en-v1.5` via the OPTIONAL `@huggingface/transformers` embedder** (lazy import; ~258MB with onnxruntime → never a hard dep; absent → actionable hint; `CMK_DISABLE_SEMANTIC=1` force-disables). **The ladder decided it (D-105 honored exactly):** spike passed first try (sqlite-vec loads on Windows via better-sqlite3; the named zvec fallback was never needed) → bench rungs: bge-small hybrid 0.765/0.800 → bge-small semantic 0.824/0.900 → bge-base hybrid 0.882/0.900 → **bge-base semantic 0.941/1.000 (R@5/paraphrase) — WINNER** → bge-m3 0.765/0.800: **the 5×-heavier multilingual giant LOST to the English-tuned base on short memory facts; the ladder found its ceiling at rung 2** (the user’s bigger-reliable-beats-small-flaky bias satisfied at minimum weight). Both bars from D-107 cleared decisively (0.529 overall, 0.300 paraphrase ceiling → 1.000). **Two honest negative results recorded:** (1) the D-72 deterministic rerank (kw 0.30/temporal 0.40) showed NO gain over raw on this corpus → built + benchmarked but NOT wired as default; (2) **semantic-raw beat hybrid-RRF** (0.941 vs 0.882) on this corpus — keyword fusion stays for exact-token robustness at scale, revisit weighting with the dogfood corpus. Architecture: content-addressed embedding cache (sha256(model+body) — the memweave pattern; only-changed re-embeds), model-derived dims (vec table auto-rebuilds on model change), the sync `semanticBackend` seam PRESERVED (async lives in `prepareSemanticBackend` — Task 120’s contract untouched); CLI + MCP auto-prepare on `--mode=semantic|hybrid`. Follow-ups (slotted): Task 46 (install opt-in for the embedder), memweave/claude-mem Phase-C dives before adopting decay/MMR/min-score, hybrid-weight revisit. _Relates Task 65/99, ADR-0002/0015, D-70/D-72/D-105/D-107._

- **📊 DECISION/NOTE (2026-06-10) — D-107: Task 99 shipped (PR #148, merged `5560d93`) — the recall benchmark exists and the baselines are MEASURED. - **🧭 DIRECTION CONFIRMED (2026-06-09) — D-104: the LLM-capture architecture is RIGHT; it's a layered hybrid, NOT "LLM-capture vs store-everything+semantic".** The user asked (concerned LLM-per-turn capture is token/context-heavy): *"are we going the right way with the llm capture? and not just taking everything, putting it in a file and then just use a semantic search?"* **Verdict: right direction.** The kit already does BOTH in layers: **(1) raw transcripts** (`context/transcripts/`) = the lossless "store everything" (proof: the async rule the grader MISSED in cut-gate7 IS in `transcripts/2026-06-09.md`); **(2) LLM auto-extract** = the curation layer that turns raw turns into small high-signal facts; **(3) semantic search over raw** (Layer 5b, v0.3) = the retrieval/safety-net. **Pure "store-everything + semantic" (naive RAG) REJECTED** because: (a) memory is INJECTED at session start into a budget-constrained coding agent — you must inject *small + high-signal*, and raw similarity chunks are noisier per token than a `**Why/How**` fact; (b) curation (deciding what's durable) IS the differentiator vs native auto-memory; (c) semantic isn't free anyway — Anthropic has no embeddings API, so it needs a local embedder (the deferred sqlite-vec). Field-validated: **mem0** (leading agent-memory) does extract-then-store + vector, NOT pure RAG. **KEY STEER for v0.3 (ties to D-103's async variance):** the per-turn grader is ~80% on AMBIGUOUSLY-phrased rules and can't be cheaply perfected — so **DON'T over-engineer the capture grader; invest v0.3 in semantic-recall-over-raw-transcripts as the backstop** (the raw already holds what the grader missed → catch misses at read-time, no extra capture tokens). Capture cost itself is tunable (Haiku already; could batch / only-substantive-turns). _Relates D-103 (async variance), Task 65/75 (v0.3 recall), design §9 (search) + §6 (auto-extract)._

  - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-99: Task 116 — coverage hardening + the persona-portability flake ROOT-CAUSED & fixed (116.x).** Two halves: **(a)** added the **★★ real-input rule** to [`cut-gate.md`](../process/cut-gate.md) — a check passes ONLY on real input; cooldown-skip / empty-queue / dry-run-nothing / same-day-nothing-to-archive = `unverified`, re-run for real (the D-84 lesson, now in the process doc, not just the decision log). The automated real-input TESTS were Tasks 112–114; live-verification was D-96/D-97. **(b) 116.x flake — found a real fragility, not just a timing race:** `rollbackImport` restored a backed-up file with `renameSync(bkp, dest)` where `dest` already held the half-applied NEW content — renaming ONTO an existing file intermittently throws EPERM/EBUSY on Windows under heavy parallel FS load, and the **fully-silent catch** then left the un-rolled-back NEW file (= the `expected 'ORIGINAL B' got 'NEW imported'` flake). **Investigation first ruled out** the cross-contamination theory (per-test mkdtemp; reindex takes explicit userDir; vitest default file-isolation; deterministic apply/rollback) → narrowed to the renameSync restore. **Fix:** `restoreBackup()` uses `copyFileSync` (reliable cross-platform overwrite) + a 5× retry for transient locks; backup removed only after a confirmed copy. 14/14 persona-portability green. **Lesson:** a "rare flake" that's silently caught is worth root-causing — this one was a genuine rollback-reliability bug (a real mid-import failure on a user's Windows box could have left a half-applied persona), not just test noise. _Relates D-84, D-93 (the flake's filing), Tasks 109–115 (the lane this hardens)._
  - **✅ SHIPPED + ✔ LIVE-VERIFIED (2026-06-08) — D-98: Task 115 — transcript temp-file hygiene (cut-gate5 H1).** The cut-gate's portability test committed a `context/transcripts/.extract-<ts>.tmp` via `git add -A` — the auto-extract turn buffer (`capture-turn.mjs:284`) isn't gitignored, so a crash-orphaned partial could travel with `git clone`. **Fix:** added `context/transcripts/.extract-*.tmp` to `template/.gitignore.fragment` (the source `cmk install` builds the managed `.gitignore` block from — install reads the fragment, not hardcoded lines). The buffer is normally consumed + deleted by the detached auto-extract child; the gitignore covers only the crash-orphan case. `cli-install.test.js` now asserts the pattern. **LIVE-verified:** scaffolded a real project, created `.extract-99999.tmp`, `git check-ignore` returned it + `git add -A` staged no `.tmp`. Minor but real (a partial extract buffer is un-Poison-Guarded raw turn content — same reason `*.extract.log` is gitignored). _Relates D-83 (the sweep that found it), Task 92 (the extract.log gitignore precedent)._

  - **🧭 DECISION (2026-06-08) — D-93: merge Task 111 on isolation-green + single-run-green; defer two PRE-EXISTING stress-only flakes to Task 116.x.** Task 111's 5× stress gate surfaced two concurrency flakes, BOTH passing in isolation + on a single clean `npm test`, BOTH unrelated to the F-2 change (auto-persona corpus/timeout): (1) `cli-capture-turn` spawn-latency under saturation — root-caused (detached child cold-start > the 3s `pollFor` window; `r.spawned` was already true) + FIXED in-PR (3s→12s); this is the exact flake PRs #22/#23 wrongly DISCLAIMED.   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-92: Task 111 — `cmk persona generate` timed out on a real project (F-2); root cause was prompt-overload, not a hang.** The cut-gate sweep first mis-reported F-2 as "PASS (cooldown)"; on a real cooldown-cleared run it errored `claude --print did not return within 50000ms`. **Root cause:** `assembleProjectCorpus` (the `facts` source) joined EVERY tier-P fact + scratchpad into ONE unbounded classifier prompt — while the SessionEnd `transcript` path was already 40KB-capped. On a project with substantial memory the prompt ballooned and Haiku blew the 50s timeout. Compounding it, the 50s was hardcoded even though `cmk persona generate` is a one-shot with NO outer hook ceiling (unlike the 60s-bounded SessionEnd path it shares `autoPersona` with). **Fix (3 parts):** (1) cap the facts corpus at `PERSONA_CORPUS_BYTES` (60KB, accumulate WHOLE facts up to budget + a truncation marker — never split a fact); (2) parameterize `autoPersona({timeoutMs})` — SessionEnd keeps the 50s default (composes with the 60s ceiling per design §8.5 / D-42), and the ceiling-free `facts` callers (`runPersonaGenerate` + `weekly-curate`) pass 120s; (3) the CLI surfaces a clear "timed out — re-run" hint instead of the raw internal error. **§8.5 composition:** the inner timeout must NOT exceed any outer ceiling — but the CLI has none, so a generous inner bound is correct there; the SessionEnd path is the one that stays 50<60. **Tests:** the "real generates candidates" test the task asked for ALREADY existed (mock backend returns `PERSONA CANDIDATE` lines, asserts `action:'promoted'` + the bullet lands in the user tier — not a cooldown-skip); added corpus-cap (Door 3: input ≤ cap + marker via `onCompress`), timeout default-vs-override, CLI 120s + hint. **Known limitation (documented):** facts past the cap drop in file-iteration order — value-ordered (trust/recency-first) accumulation is the follow-up if a large corpus drops doctrine. **Meta:** this is the 2nd of the D-84 "ran-on-trivial-input ≠ feature-works" re-audit findings to land (after Task 110); the unbounded-corpus bug only surfaced because the re-run used REAL project memory, not the empty/cooldown-skipped sweep input.

Material fix: **ARCHITECTURE.md was stale** — it still described the pre-pivot hooks (`pre-tool-memory.js` / `transcript-capture.js` / `auto-extract-memory.sh`, PreToolUse injection) and, worse, its "Why per-project, not global?" section said the kit *"doesn't share across projects automatically — copy-paste USER.md"*, directly CONTRADICTING the shipped v0.2 cross-project persona auto-promotion.
