(2) The Medium clipping "Claude Code Memory Management: The Complete Guide (2026)" (a cited source, `~` partial-verified in SOURCES.md) was misplaced at `docs/` root next to the kit's own authored docs → relocated to [`docs/sources/`](../sources/) (the zone for raw cited sources), renamed `gul-jabeen-claude-memory-guide-2026.md`, indexed in `sources/README.md`; inbound refs (SOURCES.md cites the verification note, build-log link, research-note `source:` field) updated. It is a kept source, not clutter — just home'd correctly.
  - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-90: Task 110 — `cmk forget` (and any removal) now auto-propagates to search; no manual `cmk reindex` (F-7).** **The bug (D-84 re-class):** `forget` tombstoned the fact file correctly but never touched the search index, and `reindexBoot` (which every index reader lazy-runs before reading) only ADDED/UPDATED files that still existed — it never PRUNED rows for a file that vanished. So a forgotten fact lingered in `cmk search` until a manual `reindex --full`. **Root cause:** reindexBoot was add/update-only, not a full sync. **Fix (2 parts):** (1) **reindexBoot now prunes orphans** — any `files`-checkpoint row whose source no longer exists is deleted with its observations (the FTS5 delete trigger fires per row); since `search`/`get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recent-activity` all lazy-call reindexBoot, the WHOLE deletion class (forget, queue-discard, supersede-archive, manual delete) self-heals on the next read with zero command. (2) **forget() reindexes IN-BAND** after tombstone+scrub so the index is correct the instant it returns; both `cmk forget` (CLI) + `mk_forget` (MCP) call the same `forget()`, so both surfaces get it; best-effort try/catch (the on-disk tombstone is authoritative). **Audit (trust / lessons / queue — the task asked):** NO gap — in-place edits (`trust` rewrites the file → mtime/sha1 diff → re-indexed) + adds (`lessons promote` = new source file) already self-heal via the existing lazy reindex; only DELETIONS needed the prune. Locked by a test running the REAL `overrideTrust` → `reindexBoot` chain. **inject was never broken for facts:** `injectContext` reads scratchpads (not fact files, not the index), and forget already scrubs the scratchpad bullets — the "may still be injected at SessionStart" line was a severity frame; the concrete, reproducible bug was `cmk search`. **Boundary (design §9.2.1):** a forgotten fact's row is pruned, so it's recoverable via `cmk get`/the tombstone file but NOT `cmk search --include-tombstoned` (forget = gone-from-search; the flag surfaces rows with `deleted_at` set *in the index*, which move-to-archive doesn't feed). Before this, forget left the row as a LIVE observation (`deleted_at` null) → it surfaced in DEFAULT search: the actual bug, not a working `--include-tombstoned`. **Tests:** reindexBoot orphan-prune (+over-mutation guard +no-false-positive), forget in-band (+graceful no-projectRoot), trust audit-lock. design §6.5 + §9.2.1; CHANGELOG Fixed.
  - **🐞 BUG (cut-gate5 live run, 2026-06-07) — D-81: explicit `cmk remember` SILENTLY corrupts rich facts that contain backticks.** A `--how`/`--why`/`--text`/`--title` value with backtick code-spans is eaten by **bash command-substitution** before `cmk` (node) ever reads argv → the spans are saved as empty `()`. Confirmed on disk: `feedback_use-venv-for-all-python-packages.md` How = `Create .venv if absent (), always install packages into it (), never use system pip` — both `` `python -m venv .venv` `` and `` `.\.venv\Scripts\pip install ...` `` gone; the `..venvScriptspip: command not found` line in the run is the substitution firing. **Silent** — cmk + the agent both saw success. **Blast radius:** the explicit `cmk remember` shell path only; **auto-extract (the v0.2.2 headline) is IMMUNE** (Haiku → `writeFact`, no shell). **Pre-existing** — rich `--why/--how` predates Task 103, so this lives in 0.2.1 too; NOT a v0.2.2 regression. **This is NOT R2-class / not an accept-the-edge.** The user (2026-06-07): *"this is not good at all… if this continues all our memory will be garbage… we never want this to happen."* Silent corruption of memory is the one failure a memory kit must never have. **Root cause is unrecoverable at the binary** (bash destroys the content before node starts), so the FIX must move rich content OFF the shell argv: a non-shell input channel — e.g. `cmk remember --from-file <fact.json>` (agent writes the JSON via the Write tool → zero shell parsing of content) — plus remember-skill guidance to never inline backticks/`$()`. Detection-only is weak (the evidence is already destroyed). **Owner decision PENDING:** fix as a pre-cut blocker, vs. cut v0.2.2 now (headline path immune) + fix as an immediate v0.2.3 fast-follow task. Needs a §16 design candidate + a cut-gate known-edge note once the fix shape is settled.

Scope: (a) fix D-81 resiliently — CLI `remember --from-file <fact.json>` + `--json -` (stdin) → `JSON.parse` → the SAME structured object the MCP tool passes; rich content never touches argv, so `fs.readFileSync`+`JSON.parse` is byte-total; (b) close the CLI↔MCP drift — MCP gains the write/mutate tools, CLI gains `get`/`timeline`/`cite`/`recent-activity` (the 4 read verbs it lacks today), both as thin adapters over the shared core; (c) a `validate-cli-mcp-parity.mjs` guard wired into `npm test`. **Decision-1 (APPROVED):** MCP gets the destructive ops too, but `forget`/`purge` over MCP require an explicit **confirm-token param** (mirrors CLI `--yes`) so the auto-invoking model can't silently tombstone. NOT Cursor/Kiro/ChatGPT/Antigravity (closed or spec-methodology-only — no studiable dual-surface code for THIS question). **CHECKED-AND-EXCLUDED for THIS question (2026-06-07, real-repo verify):** `memory-os` (ClaudioDrews) — a backend memory-OS for the Hermes agent (Docker/Qdrant/Redis/ARQ), **no standalone CLI, no MCP** (integrates only via the Hermes Icarus plugin hooks), so nothing to teach on CLI↔MCP parity or shell-safe input; it stays relevant only to Task 75 (authoritative-injection) + Task 97 (dynamic trust), already filed. Our existing `docs/research/` notes answer the CAPTURE question, not the CLI-MCP-parity + shell-safe-input question, so this is net-new research. **Honesty note (the assistant, 2026-06-07):** I do NOT already know their live source — prior citations were from our notes (some code-level, some survey); training data on these niche products is unreliable.   - **🧭 PRODUCT PRINCIPLE (binding, 2026-06-07) — D-85: the regular user NEVER runs a `cmk` command — they live in free speech.** Every memory operation reaches the kit one of two ways: **AUTOMATIC** (hooks — capture / inject / compress / auto-extract / persona-promotion — the user does nothing) or **CLAUDE-MEDIATED** (the user voices an intent — *"forget the API key"*, *"what did we decide about X"*, *"always use uv"* — and Claude translates it into the kit action via a skill trigger or an MCP tool). **The `cmk` CLI is Claude's + power-users' tool, NEVER the regular user's interface** — if a regular user ever has to type `cmk` or run `reindex`, the kit failed. Consequences: (a) every user-expressible intent MUST have an automatic OR Claude-mediated path — a CLI verb with no skill-trigger / MCP-tool is **invisible** to the regular user; (b) once triggered, the action must **complete automatically** (F-7 / Task 110: *"forget X"* → gone from search AND inject, zero follow-up command); (c) the **MCP tool surface + skill layer IS the real user-facing surface** (via Claude) — so Task 108's CLI↔MCP parity is the *free-speech action surface*, not symmetry-for-its-own-sake. **Gaps today (intents with NO reliable free-speech path):** *"forget X"* (no forget skill/tool — memory-write is remember-only; MCP has no `mk_forget`), *"trust this / not important"* (none), reliable recall-on-a-question (partial — Task 75 active-recall). → **Task 117.** Source: the user 2026-06-07: *"the regular user will not run commands, at all… they assume that if they tell Claude in free speech, then it will happen or it happened automatic… this is what they think about every command."* **Clinching evidence (same day): the MAINTAINER himself drove this entire cut-gate CLI sweep by telling Claude *"if you think we should run all the commands we didnt run, you could do it"* — then *"even i dont run commands and tell you to do it."* Even the author, who knows every command exists, uses free-speech→Claude rather than typing `cmk`. So the model is UNIVERSAL, not a novice accommodation — the conversation IS the interface for everyone; the CLI is the substrate Claude drives.** Graduates toward a design principle + CLAUDE.md.
  - **♻️ REVISIT (2026-06-07) — D-80 (R2 `cd`-compound permission edge) gets its "simple solution" via Task 108's MCP-first surface.** D-80 parked R2 ("won't fix unless a simple solution arrives") because the bash path is un-allowlistable — Claude Code matches a compound `cd "…" && cmk …` PER-SUBCOMMAND, so the `cd &&` prefix dodges `Bash(cmk:*)`. **New evidence (the user, 2026-06-07):** the MCP path dissolves it by construction — an `mk_*` call is a JSON-RPC tool, NOT a shell command, so there's no `cd`, no compound, no `Bash()` matcher; and the MCP server already knows the project root (launched per `.mcp.json`). **Simple fix (rides Task 108):** `cmk install` allowlists `mcp__cmk__*` (mirroring the existing `Bash(cmk *)` + `Skill(memory-write)` allowlists from Tasks 79/90) → the Claude-mediated path is pre-approved, ZERO prompts, none of the 3 rejected hacks (`Bash(cd:*)` / leading-`*` wildcard / PreToolUse hook).   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🎓 LESSON (2026-06-07) — D-86: Task 108a merged (PR #130); real-binary subprocess tests don't count for line coverage — extract pure, dep-injected helpers.** 108a (`cmk remember --from-file`/`--json` — the **D-81** fix: rich content read from a file/stdin never touches the shell) shipped. **The lesson (reusable):** the PR's SonarCloud gate failed at *"12.5% coverage on new code"* even though the `--from-file`/`--json` logic was thoroughly tested — because the kit's CLI tests spawn the **real binary** (`spawnSync(cmk.mjs)`, Door 3), and a subprocess's execution is invisible to the parent process's coverage instrumentation. **The fix is also better design:** extract the logic into a PURE, dependency-injected helper (`parseFactInput`) + make the action dep-injectable (`runRemember(…, {projectRoot, log, logError})`, mirroring `runRememberRich`) and unit-test those **in-process**; keep the real-binary test for the wiring (Door 3). **Apply going forward:** when new CLI logic is only real-binary-tested, add in-process unit tests on an extracted pure helper / dep-injected action — don't rely on the subprocess test for coverage. Two-pass review fixes also landed (field allowlist so a crafted JSON can't forge provenance, 64 KB input cap, `readHookStdin` reuse, bare-remember guard).   - **✅ SHIPPED + 🐞 FIX (2026-06-08) — D-89: Task 109 — `cmk register-crons` fixed on Windows (broken since v0.1) + a macOS sibling bug found & fixed.** D-83's bug: the win32 path built schtasks as a pre-quoted shell string `/TR "${command}"` where `command` = the quoted path triple `"<node>" "<script>" "<projectRoot>"` (Task 36 B1/B2) — so the inner quotes double-wrapped AND `registerCron`'s own guard *rejected* the `"` → cron could NEVER register on Windows (even `--dry-run`, exit 2). **Root-cause class:** a single pre-quoted command STRING can't serve three platforms' quoting — Linux nests it in `echo '…'`, Windows re-wraps in `/TR "…"`, macOS splits on whitespace. **Fix:** win32 now execs `schtasks` with an ARGS ARRAY (no `shell:true`) → the `/TR` value reaches schtasks verbatim (CreateProcess arg-quoting); cmd.exe parses the quoted paths only when the task FIRES. Removed the self-contradictory double-quote rejection; `buildWindowsSchtasks` returns + exports the argv array, unit-tested via a new `platform` test seam on `registerCron` (since `detectPlatform()` can't vary on a single CI host — the gap that let this ship). **macOS sibling, found the same pass:** the plist `command.split(/\s+/)` kept the wrapping quotes → `<string>"/path/node"</string>` → launchd exec'd a literally-quoted path → ENOENT. Silently broken, never reported because the crons were never checked since v0.1 (the user: *"we didn't check the crons since the first version"*). Now strips the wrapping quotes. Linux was already correct. **HC-6:** no change needed — once the command works, its "Run `cmk register-crons`" advice is valid (it already points at the lazy-on-read fallback too). **Remaining edge (backlog, v0.2.x):** a node/project path that itself contains a SPACE breaks the macOS whitespace-split — the real fix is the `command:string` → `argv:string[]` API refactor (each platform quotes from raw argv); rare for node/project paths, so not a blocker. **Lesson:** dry-run-only tests + a "platform-tested by the user at install" Door-3 N/A note let a broken Windows AND macOS path ship for two minor versions — cross-platform builders must be tested directly (pure functions, platform-seam-injected), not deferred to manual install-time checks.

- **D-80 NOTE (2026-06-07) — explicit-capture R2 prompt on a `cd <abs-path> && cmk` compound is a KNOWN, ACCEPTED edge — DOCUMENTED, deliberately NOT fixed. SETTLED.** The user (2026-06-07): *"lets just document it as an edge case we wont 'fix' unless we have a working simple solution."* Surfaced by the v0.2.2 cut-gate live run: the agent captured a preference richly (`cmk remember "…" --type feedback --why … --how … --title …`, no "remember this" — F1 working) but Claude Code popped *"Allow this bash command?"* because the agent wrapped it as `cd "c:/Temp/cut-gate5" && cmk remember …`. **Verified root cause against the primary source ([code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions)):** (1) `cd` is a built-in **read-only** command (auto-approved) — but only when the target is *inside the working directory*; a `cd` to an **absolute path** Claude Code doesn't recognize as inside the WD doesn't qualify. (2) Compounds are **split per-subcommand** ("a rule must match each subcommand independently") — so the whole `cd … && cmk …` prompts because the `cd`-to-absolute-path subcommand didn't qualify, NOT because of `cmk`. (3) `Bash(cmk:*)` (≡ `Bash(cmk *)`) already covers the **bare** `cmk remember …` — which is the normal case → no prompt. So **R2 substantially passes**; the friction is only the agent's redundant `cd <abs>` wrapper. **Two false fixes ruled out by the docs (verify-before-shipping paid off):** `Bash(cd:*)` is a **no-op** (cd is already read-only); `Bash(*cmk:*)` doesn't help (the `cmk` subcommand already matches; the `cd` subcommand is the issue) AND would be a hole. **Why we're NOT fixing:** the only two real options both have a catch — a behavioral skill/CLAUDE.md nudge ("run `cmk` directly, never `cd` first") which the docs themselves say *"doesn't change what Claude Code allows"* (the weak kind), OR a **PreToolUse hook** to auto-approve `cmk` capture calls (the docs' endorsed mechanism) which **re-opens ADR-0006's deliberate PreToolUse-drop** ("fires on every tool invocation") — an architectural decision, not a quick patch. **Trigger to revisit:** a *simple, reliable* solution (e.g. if Claude Code later treats `cd`-to-WD-root as read-only in all forms, or a cheap non-PreToolUse mechanism appears). Filed as a deferred candidate (design §16.57). _Relates R2 cut-gate check, ADR-0006 (PreToolUse drop), Task 79/90 (cmk + skill allow-listing), the v0.2.2 cut-gate; primary source verified._

- **D-79 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 106: the §16.27 `now.md` compress race is CLOSED via the file-rename pattern (for BOTH callers). SETTLED.** Surfaced by Task 105 self-review (D-78): `compressSession` read `now.md` → ~5–10s Haiku → `truncateSync(0)`, so a turn the (new) session appended in that window was dropped. **Fix:** `compressSession` now CLAIMS the buffer by atomic rename (`now.md → now.md.rolling-{ts}`) before the Haiku call (`claimNowBuffer`), compresses the claimed copy, and on success `discardRolling` (unlink) — `now.md` is owned by the session's appenders, never re-touched, so a concurrent append is never clobbered. On Haiku failure/timeout, `restoreRolling` puts the un-compressed buffer back (prepended to anything appended meanwhile), preserving the old "leave now.md intact → retry next roll" contract. **Design decisions:** (1) **Pure rename, no re-create** — an uncontended roll leaves `now.md` ABSENT (not truncate-to-0-bytes); re-creating an empty `now.md` would re-open a (tiny) clobber race against a concurrent append, so we don't. The 3 honesty/unit tests asserting `size === 0` were corrected to "no leftover (empty OR absent)" — exactly the size-vs-existence correction §16.27 had predicted (the note claimed the tests would survive unchanged; they needed this one-line contract correction, which is consistent with the note's INTENT: pin the OUTCOME, not the impl). (2) **Restore-on-error prepends** (claimed buffer is older → leads) so both the un-rolled buffer + any concurrent append survive. (3) **`cmk roll --scope now` inherits it free** (it delegates to `compressSession`). **Verified:** a deterministic race test (backend appends mid-compress; the turn must survive + error-path restore + no orphan rolling file) + a **12/12 live-Haiku end-to-end run** (real `claude --print`: a turn appended ~1.5s into the real Haiku call survived while the prior content rolled). **Honesty correction carried from D-78:** D-78's first claim "the §16.27 race composes fine" was WRONG; this task is the fix, and the corrected D-78 line + §16.27 both reflect that. _Relates §16.27 (now SHIPPED), D-78, Task 105, Task 27 (I4, the original §16.27 finding), `compress-session.mjs`._

- **D-78 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 105: the now→today roll now ALSO fires lazily at SessionStart, so rolling compression no longer depends on a clean SessionEnd. SETTLED (implements the D-75 fix).** D-75 found the `now.md` → `today-{date}.md` roll (`compressSession`) was SessionEnd-only, and Claude Code fires SessionEnd only on a clean window-close — so a never-cleanly-closed session left `now.md` unbounded with no `today-*.md`/`recent.md`. Fix: `detectStaleness` gains a `stale-now` verdict (now.md `trim() !== ''`) at **highest precedence after cron/no-context-dir**; `runLazyCompress` dispatches it to `compressSession`; `inject-context` adds `stale-now` to its detached-spawn condition. **Design decisions:** (1) **Detached, not inline** — a Haiku roll can't run in the 500ms SessionStart budget, so THIS session injects pre-roll state and the next gets the rolled state (the standard §8.2.1 lazy tradeoff; the spec's "roll THEN inject" wording is aspirational — the real mechanism mirrors the already-working daily-distill lazy pattern). (2) **One-verdict-one-cycle, cascading** — `stale-now` takes precedence over weekly/daily because now→today is the FIRST pipeline level; the today→recent + weekly levels self-heal on subsequent SessionStarts once now.md drains. (3) **Cooldown composes** — `runLazyCompress` gates 120s up front and passes `cooldownMs:0` to the inner `compressSession`, so a clean SessionEnd immediately followed by a reopen doesn't double-roll. (4) **Scope: now→today ONLY** — MEMORY.md graduation already has a reactive-on-write path (Task 94), so it never grew unbounded; the now-roll was the *unique* gap, so Task 105 does NOT add graduation to the lazy path. **§16.27 race — does NOT fully compose (self-review finding, corrected):** my first read said "the roll fires at session start, before the new session's appends, so it composes fine." Deeper review proved that WRONG — `compressSession` reads now.md, spends ~5–10s in Haiku, then truncates to 0, so a turn appended by the NEW session during that window is dropped from `today-*.md`. It's MORE likely than the SessionEnd §16.27 case (a starting session actively appends; an ending one doesn't) and opens a minor new loss path (the dropped turn is transcript-recoverable, not durable-memory loss; and timing usually avoids it — the first append lands after the ~10s roll). Net still strongly positive (before Task 105 now.md grew UNBOUNDED). Documented in §16.27 as the concrete "visible user pain" trigger for the file-rename fix (§16.27 candidate #1) — recommended as a focused follow-up PR (the rename touches the shared compressSession + needs a race test). **Read-the-docs-first note:** the user asked mid-task whether I'd read the rolling-compression docs first; I read design §8 + §8.2.1/.2 + §16.27 + D-75 BEFORE writing implementation — and the §16.27 read is exactly what flagged this race on self-review. _Relates D-75, Task 35 (lazy-compress mechanism this extends), Task 86c (SessionEnd persona pass — still SessionEnd-only, a known smaller gap), design §8.1/§8.2.2, §16.27 (now.md truncate race — file-rename follow-up)._

- **D-77 DECISION (2026-06-07) — Task 103: `cmk-auto-extract` now synthesizes RICH Why/How fact files on the native-immune Stop-hook path. SETTLED.** Implements the D-74 fix: rich capture rode ONLY the explicit `cmk remember` path, which native Auto Memory can hijack (winner-take-all); the immune Stop-hook auto-extract wrote only terse bullets. Now the SAME per-turn Haiku pass (no second LLM call) emits a third output type — a fenced `BEGIN_FACT…END_FACT` block for durable project KNOWLEDGE (triggers 3–6: setup/config, conventions, workflows, quirks) — routed via `writeFact` to the fact store. Lighter signals (triggers 1–2) stay terse `MEMORY.md` bullets. **Four design decisions, all settled:** (1) **trust:medium** (spec-settled) — auto-extract is a Haiku synthesis = proposal-grade; explicit `cmk remember` stays high + supersedes. (2) **Direct-to-fact-store, NOT the review queue** — deliberate deviation from the terse "medium → queue" convention; the point is *automatic* native-parity capture (native writes its files with no approval step), the fact store is searchable-but-not-full-trust-injected, writeFact screens every write, and explicit-high supersedes. (3) **Rich-vs-terse split + XOR** — each fact is EITHER a rich block OR a terse line (prompt-enforced; a terse candidate whose canonical id matches a rich fact's body is dropped as a safety net). (4) **Shared `rich-fact.mjs`** — `buildRichFactBody`+`slugifyFact` extracted from `subcommands.mjs` so explicit + automatic paths build identical files. **It's BOTH/AND (D-74 addendum):** git-portability/provenance/3-tier STAY differentiators; this makes the memory itself native-parity-then-better — the LIVE parity check confirmed real Haiku emits a STRUCTURED body (Architectural Pattern + Tech Stack breakdown) + Why/How that matches/beats native. **Parser robustness surfaced by that live check:** Haiku formats multi-line bodies as a YAML block scalar (`body: |` + indent) → `cleanFieldValue` strips the indicator + dedents (a mocked test would never have caught this — the manual live check earned its keep). REJECTED (still): PreToolUse hard-block + disable-native-default (D-74). _Relates D-74, Task 21/23 (auto-extract), Task 63 (rich capture), ADR-0011, design §6.4 (rich-fact synthesis), the §19 graduation composition (rich facts land in the graduation TARGET, reducing scratchpad pressure)._

- **FIX (2026-06-07) — Task 101: extended the manual-run stdin-hang fix (Task 100) from `cmk-compress-session` to ALL hook bins.** Every hook bin drained stdin with a raw blocking `readFileSync(0)` that hangs forever on a manual TTY run (no piped payload → the console never sends EOF), before any body runs — the same class Task 100 fixed for only the SessionEnd bin. Routed `cmk-capture-prompt`, `cmk-capture-turn`, `cmk-inject-context`, `cmk-observe-edit` (npm + plugin twins) and the plugin-only `cmk-version-check` through the existing `readHookStdin({ isTTY: process.stdin.isTTY })` helper (returns `''` for a TTY). Each bin loads the helper via the SAME guarded dynamic-import block as its main module, so a corrupt install still emits its hook envelope + exit 0 (graceful-degradation preserved); plugin `observe-edit` keeps its envelope-FIRST ordering via a split import (drain-helper before the envelope, heavy append module after). Regression-locked by `tests/cli-hook-stdin-drain.test.js` — structural (every bin delegates to the helper, injects `isTTY`, and contains no raw `readFileSync(0)`) + behavioral (empty stdin exits 0 within a hard timeout). **`cmk-compress-session` folded into the structural lock too** — the user caught the "out of scope" framing on its leftover comment token: it wasn't out of scope, the test just hadn't covered the already-fixed bin (lazy-framing class, corrected). _Relates Task 100, NFR-5 spirit, the twin-bin lockstep hazard._

- **D-76 FIX (2026-06-07) — `cli-index-rebuild.test.js` 29.4 #2 ("boot after editing one fact") was a load-induced mtime-granularity flake (stress 4/5); made deterministic with `utimesSync`.** `reindexBoot`'s fast path skips files whose `floor(mtimeMs)` matches the indexed checkpoint (intentional + documented — a content change that preserves mtime isn't re-read). The test seeds a fact, boots, then edits + boots again expecting `filesReindexed === 1`; it writes the seed and the edit <1ms apart, so under 5x stress the two mtimes collided → fast-path skip → `filesReindexed === 0`. **Test fix, not code fix (stated explicitly per the anti-pattern rule):** the production fast-path is correct by design (it avoids re-reading every file's content on every boot — a deliberate perf choice); the test was relying on the wall clock advancing between two synchronous writes, which isn't guaranteed under load. Forced a strictly-later mtime on the edited file (`utimesSync(factPath, now+10s)`) to simulate the real-world edit-gap. Surfaced as a Task 101 stress detour — problem-forced, and structurally unrelated to the hook-bin change (the test imports `reindexBoot`, never a hook bin). _Relates `index-rebuild.mjs` mtime caveat, the stress-gate non-jitter rule, D-68 (stress logging that NAMED the failing test)._

- **D-75 FINDING (2026-06-06) — rolling compression (`now.md` → `today-*.md`) is SessionEnd-only, and Claude Code fires SessionEnd ONLY on a clean window-close, not on new-chat-same-window → it silently never ran in the not-cleanly-closed cut-gate runs. NOT a wedge blocker; fix = Task 105 (lazy-roll on SessionStart).** Surfaced at the cut-gate Session-1→2 boundary. **What's verified:** the SessionEnd chain WORKS — on a clean close of `mem-test3` it fired fully (Haiku `compressSession` → accurate `today-2026-06-06.md` summary, `now.md` 10 KB→0, the §19 graduation sweep, and `context/sessions/{date}.compress.log`, all at 21:02). **But across cut-gate2 + cut-gate3** (never cleanly closed) `now.md` accumulated ~10 KB/22 turns over multiple sessions and **never rolled** — no `today-*.md`, no `recent.md`, no Task-86c SessionEnd persona pass. The wedge still worked there because the **Stop-hook inline path** (capture + persona) is independent of SessionEnd. **Consequence if a user never cleanly exits:** unbounded `now.md`, no injected rolling summary (`recent.md`), no 86c second-grade for queued persona candidates. **Fix (Task 105):** lazy-roll a stale `now.md` at SessionStart (in `cmk-inject-context`), mirroring the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart precedent; keep the SessionEnd path too (idempotent). **Self-correction logged (5th of this thread):** the assistant first reported "`compress.log` empty everywhere → SessionEnd never fired" — but was looking in `context/.locks/`; the compress log actually lives at **`context/sessions/{date}.compress.log`**. The *conclusion* (no compression before the clean close) held, but the path claim was wrong — verify the artifact location before asserting absence. _Relates Task 105, Task 86c (SessionEnd persona pass), §6 (rolling-window compression), the daily-distill lazy-on-SessionStart precedent; surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate._

- **D-74 FINDING (2026-06-06) — a cut-gate run captured to Claude's NATIVE Auto Memory instead of the kit; investigation says VARIANCE not regression, and the whole field captures via the Stop hook (immune). NOT a v0.2.0 blocker. Full write-up: [research note](../research/2026-06-06-native-auto-memory-coexistence-investigation.md).** In `cut-gate3` (Claude Code v2.1.167) the agent saved stated preferences to Claude Code's **native Auto Memory** (`Write ~/.claude/projects/<slug>/memory/feedback_*.md`) and **never called `cmk remember`** — the kit's `context/memory/` ended up empty, vs `cut-gate2` which produced 3 rich `cmk remember` fact files. **Verdict (decisive): VARIANCE, not regression.** A same-version re-run (`mem-test3`, also v2.1.167) used the kit correctly (`cmk remember --why/--how` → rich fact file, no native). Same version → both outcomes ⇒ the host-version-causation theory is dead (the assistant leaned on it twice, too confidently; the maintainer pushed back; the primary source — [code.claude.com/docs/en/memory](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/memory) + changelog — shows native is the agent writing notes itself, on by default since v2.1.59, **no documented behavior change in 2.1.160–2.1.167**, and CLAUDE.md is *"context, not enforced configuration"* that *"won't reliably hold"*). **What's at risk when native wins a turn is BOUNDED:** the kit's Stop-hook `cmk-auto-extract` captured the cross-project persona (5 promotions) + terse `MEMORY.md` bullets in `cut-gate3` anyway — the **wedge is immune by construction** (the hook reads the conversation; the agent's tool choice is irrelevant). Only the **rich project fact files** are lost (auto-extract writes terse; only explicit `cmk remember` writes rich Why/How). **What the field does (10 competitor READMEs fetched + our deep-dives):** NONE disable native; NONE even mention it (MemPalace/supermemory explicitly "complement"); the **entire field captures ONLY via the Stop hook** (memsearch/claude-mem/claude-remember/Hermes) with **no agent-invoked "remember" command** — so native has nothing to compete with. Our `cmk-auto-extract` is the *same shape*; the kit's explicit `cmk remember` is an *addition* (our differentiator) and the *only* surface native can win. **DECISION:** (1) **ADR-0011 coexist-default STANDS** — the case for disable-by-default is *weaker* than it looked (intermittent + costs only the rich-fact tier); make `cmk disable-native-memory` prominent/recommended instead. (2) **Real fix = Task 103:** enrich `cmk-auto-extract` to write rich fact files so rich capture rides the immune Stop-hook path; explicit `cmk remember` becomes a bonus and native winning a turn costs nothing. (3) A PreToolUse hard-block (the only *forced* redirect) was **REJECTED by the user (2026-06-06)** — intercepting Claude Code's own tool calls is too invasive/fragile for an intermittent loss of the least-critical tier; do NOT re-propose it. **Honesty note:** logged the twice-over-reached version theory deliberately — correlation-as-cause is the lazy-framing class; `mem-test3` (same version, kit won) is the empirical disproof. _Relates ADR-0011, Task 103 (enrich auto-extract), Task 60 (`disable-native-memory`), Task 21/23 (auto-extract), Task 63 (rich capture), the 2026-06-06 competitor README survey._
  - **Addendum — two strategic directives (the user 2026-06-06), both binding:**
    1. **It's WINNER-TAKE-ALL, not coexistence (corrects the FINDING's softer framing).** The cross-tab is exclusive: kit fact files **XOR** native files, never both (cut-gate 4/0, cut-gate2 3/0, cut-gate3 0/5, mem-test3 1/0). When one wins the explicit save, the other writes **nothing** that session. (The kit's always-on auto-extract still runs underneath — that's why the persona fills regardless — but the explicit-save layer is exclusive.) Native ALSO now writes rich Why/How fact files (side-by-side: native's `user_backend_philosophy.md` was MORE structured than our one-shot `cmk remember`) — **our v0.1.1 "we capture richer" moat is GONE.**
    2. **Memory QUALITY must lead — but it's BOTH/AND, not either/or.** The user: *"leaning on this 3 [git-portability / citation-IDs / provenance] are idiotic cause this project is supposed to deliver memory, not gimmicks"* — clarified 2026-06-06 to *"it's not wrong, we didn't say we're not doing that also; it's not mutually exclusive."* So the 3 **STAY real differentiators** (native is machine-local + ephemeral → structurally can't do them) — they are NOT dropped. The correction is narrower: don't pitch the win **solely** on them while the memory itself lags. **Keep the differentiators AND make capture+recall native-parity-then-better.** Task 103's bar reflects this.
  - **SHIP-CADENCE reaffirmed (the user 2026-06-06; reaffirms D-24/25/26).** *"are we ever going to publish 0.2 or do every task until the youtube idea?"* → **Ship v0.2.0 now** (per the one-wow-per-version cadence); the native investigation is NOT a blocker (variance). Task 103/104 are v0.2.x/v0.3, AFTER the tag. Sequence: finish the cut-gate ★s → tag v0.2.0 → then Task 103. Do not treadmill tasks before publishing. **Filed:** Task 104 (transcript fidelity for the recall waterfall — expand OUR transcript, never copy Anthropic's JSONL; L3 last-resort semantic-search tier, MemPalace-style; driven by Q1 of this investigation — the JSONL is complete but machine-local + ~30-day-expiry, so neither portable nor durable)._

- **ISSUE (2026-06-06) — `cmk-compress-session` TIMES OUT (exit 124, ~60s) on the real global install when the SessionEnd Haiku passes have input; the proactive graduation sweep (Task 94.3) then never runs. NEEDS INVESTIGATION (potential v0.2.0 blocker — do NOT tag until resolved).** Surfaced by the v0.2.0 cut-gate deterministic probes (B7). Repro: `cmk install` a throwaway, `cmk remember` ~14 facts, lower `MEMORY.md` cap below current size (but **above** the ~1146 B scaffold floor, e.g. 1400), `CMK_PROJECT_DIR=<dir> timeout 60 cmk-compress-session` → **exit 124, MEMORY unchanged, 0 session-end graduated events, ZERO stderr** (hung before `summarizeSessionEnd` printed). **What's confirmed working:** empty-project compress-session = fast skip/skip/graduation (exit 0); **reactive** graduation on write (B5) = ✅ 9 graduated on the real install; cmk-compress-session does NOT hang in general. **The hang correlates with the Haiku pass having input** (fact corpus / transcript) → it spawns `claude --print`, and the test shell has **no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / no Claude auth** → the spawn hangs. **CORRECTION (the no-auth theory was WRONG):** the kit's Haiku backend is **`claude --print`** (authed by the Claude **subscription** / logged-in CLI, NOT `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`). Verified `echo … | claude --print --model haiku` → replies fast, **exit 0** in this same shell. So the hang is **NOT** the Haiku spawn / auth. **Corrected lead:** the hang appears only when **graduation does REAL work** (over-cap with eligible bullets → `writeFact` → `reindex` per bullet); the empty case (graduation 0) is fast. **Prime suspect = the reindex/index path or a lock**, NOT Haiku — and note the maintainer has **memsearch 0.4.3 installed but Milvus almost certainly NOT running** (HC-7: "milvus reachability is Layer 5b"), so a reindex/writeFact step that touches memsearch/Milvus could block. **NEXT STEP for the resuming session:** (1) read `reindex.mjs` + `write-fact.mjs` + `graduation.mjs` — does graduation's per-bullet `writeFact`→`reindex` shell out to `memsearch`/Milvus or take a lock that can hang? (2) repro with memsearch removed / `CMK_SKIP_*` to isolate; (3) confirm whether `runSessionEndTasks` printed NO stderr because it hung in graduation (after the concurrent block) vs in the Haiku passes — add/inspect a per-stage log; (4) fix before tagging v0.2.0. _Earlier (a)/(b) Haiku-timeout framing is SUPERSEDED by this correction; the `claude --print` spawn is fine._ **CORRECTION #2 — memsearch is ALSO ruled out (grep is decisive):** `reindex.mjs`/`write-fact.mjs`/`graduation.mjs`/`index-db.mjs`/`index-rebuild.mjs` only do `db.exec(...)` (SQLite FTS5) — **no `memsearch`, no Milvus, no `spawn`/`child_process`.** The kit's ONLY memsearch reference is `doctor.mjs` HC-1 (`spawnBinSync('memsearch',['--version'])` for detection). So the graduation→reindex path is **pure SQLite** — memsearch/Milvus is NOT the cause; do NOT uninstall memsearch (won't help; the test suite mocks HC-1 anyway). **Remaining suspects (narrowed):** (1) a **lock** — the 14 `cmk remember` writes + the SessionEnd writes contending in `lock-discipline.mjs` / `.locks/`; (2) the **better-sqlite3 reindex** blocking on a locked/large index DB during the per-bullet `writeFact`→`reindex` loop; (3) `autoPersona` making a real (slow but valid) `claude --print` pass over the 14-fact corpus. **NEXT: add a per-stage timing/log to `runSessionEndTasks` (or run compress/persona/graduation in isolation on the repro) to see which of the three actually blocks; the zero-stderr means it never reached `summarizeSessionEnd`.** Other deterministic checks PASSED: G2/G3/G4, B5, C3 (poison exit 2, 0 leak), C4 (0 username leak, ~ shown), F-3b persona export/import (exit 0, 0 leak). _Relates Task 94.3 (proactive sweep), design §8.5 (inner-timeout/kill-chain composition), PR-A (the same class), the v0.2.0 gate._

- **FIX / RESOLVED (2026-06-06) — root cause was the bin BLOCKING ON STDIN, not graduation/Haiku/lock/memsearch. All four earlier theories were wrong because they assumed the bin's BODY ran — it never did.** `cmk-compress-session.mjs` (both twin bins) drains stdin via `readFileSync(0, 'utf8')` at the very top (then `void`s it — the content is discarded; the read only exists to drain the hook pipe). When the bin is invoked MANUALLY without redirecting stdin — exactly what the B7 probe does (`cmk-compress-session | Out-Null` pipes stdout but leaves stdin on the interactive console, which never sends EOF) — `readFileSync(0)` blocks forever, before compress/persona/graduation ever run. The 60s SessionEnd hook ceiling then kills it → **exit 124, MEMORY unchanged, 0 graduated events, ZERO stderr** (it never reached `summarizeSessionEnd` because it never reached ANY of the body). In the REAL hook this never happens: Claude Code pipes the hook JSON to stdin → `readFileSync(0)` gets EOF → returns instantly (this is why "empty project = fast" — those runs had stdin fed). **Decisive evidence:** (a) repro of the full SessionEnd pipeline against repo source with per-stage timing = **47ms total** (compress skip/empty, persona skip/no-transcript, graduation 5 graduated in 39ms) — NO hang; (b) the installed global bin with stdin=`/dev/null` (EOF) → exit 0, full output, ~0ms; with stdin=a pipe that never EOFs → **exit 124** (blocked). The maintainer was right the install is NOT stale (uninstall+reinstall from main); the staleness theory (a 5th) was also wrong. **FIX:** (1) extract the stdin drain into a testable `readHookStdin({ isTTY })` helper that returns `''` when stdin is a TTY (interactive) instead of blocking; both twin bins call it — a manual run now degrades gracefully. (2) cut-gate B7 probe feeds stdin (`'{}' | cmk-compress-session`). **LESSON:** four theories chased the code I was READING; none reproduced first. The reproduce-with-instrumentation step (47ms) falsified all of them in one shot and pointed at the bin wrapper — which I'd skimmed past because `void rawInput` made the read look inert. _The v0.2.0 gate is now UNBLOCKED pending the helper PR._

All deterministic ★s pass (F-3 promote, H1 clone-has-committed-memory). Findings → fixes: (1) **search-id vs fact-id wart** — `cmk search` lists ids for BOTH facts AND scratchpad bullets, but `lessons promote`/`forget` act on facts only → a pasted bullet id gave a flat "no matching fact". **Fixed (Task 102, PR #124):** `bullet-lookup.mjs` + actionable errors. (2) **cut-gate doc drift** — the guide listed v0.1.x stubs (`cmk view`, bare `cmk compress`, `cmk purge --hard`, `cmk config get/set`) as runnable, omitted `forget --yes`, and showed `transcripts extract <file>` (it takes 0 args and crawls the WHOLE `~/.claude/projects` history — many MB). **Fixed (docs commit `1bae70f`):** stubs marked "expect not-yet-implemented", `--yes` added, F-15 0-arg scope flagged. **NOT fixed (intentional):** the stubs themselves stay v0.1.x deferrals (design §16); `transcripts extract`'s whole-history crawl is the feature, now documented. The F-sweep is best run AFTER the interactive wedge against the real `cut-gate3` (it has real auto-extracted facts), not a throwaway — synthetic data only proves the commands don't crash. _Relates Task 102, Task 76/9, the v0.2.0 cut-gate._

Note: [2026-06-06-recall-deep-dive-graphiti-mem0-memoryos.md](../research/2026-06-06-recall-deep-dive-graphiti-mem0-memoryos.md). **#4 Graphiti (Task 66):** it's **bi-temporal** — `valid_at`/`invalid_at` (world truth) + `created_at`/`expired_at` (system knowledge). **Conclusion: we need only the TRUTH axis in frontmatter; the system axis we already get FREE from git history + audit.log** → single-axis-frontmatter + git = our bi-temporal, *less* to build than a triple store. **#5 mem0 (Task 95/F-D):** signature = a batched LLM "memory manager" deciding **ADD/UPDATE/DELETE/NONE** per fact vs existing memory (its `DEFAULT_UPDATE_MEMORY_PROMPT` is a ready template). **Conclusion: fold that op-set into the Task-95 reviewable re-curation pass** (handles "Postgres→SQLite" as UPDATE/supersede); keep per-write deterministic (zero-API). **#6 memory-os (Task 75/97):** Layer-07 "Ground Truth Hierarchy" — **its problem statement is our cold-open failure verbatim** ("agent ignores injected memory, treats every question as novel"). **Near-copyable fix for Task 75.0:** a ranked source hierarchy in `SOUL.md` (terminal > injected-memory > official-docs > training) + the key line *"injected memory wins… never treat a question as novel when the answer is already in your prompt."* Its **dynamic-trust is NOT a re-confirm bump** (corrects our README read, D-64) — it's **source-confidence init (0.85 curated / 0.70 session) + `last_accessed_at` decay/archive** → for Task 97: bump `last_accessed` on recall, make staleness **access-aware not pure-age**. **Everything stays our shape** — committed markdown, sqlite-vec+FTS5, no server, no per-write LLM; took algorithms, rejected all infra (Milvus/Chroma/Neo4j/Qdrant/Redis/Docker). - **D-69 FIX — Task 72 CORE shipped: `cmk persona export` / `import` give the cross-project persona a portability button (per-human, not per-repo). SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-72-persona-portability).** Closes the D-27 honesty gap: the wedge implied "portable across machines," but only PROJECT memory (committed `context/`) travelled — the persona (user tier) is machine-local + deliberately OUT of the repo (committing it leaks your working-style to teammates). **Built (72.1):** [persona-portability.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/persona-portability.mjs) — `exportPersona` packs the user tier into one OS-agnostic JSON bundle via an **allow-list** (USER/HABITS/LESSONS + settings.json + fragments/ + queues/; runtime `.locks/.index/.import-backups` are NEVER bundled — allow-list not deny-list, so a future runtime dir can't leak in); `importPersona` **overwrites** (the explicit primitive has no merge — that's the deferred git-sync path) but backs up every replaced file to `.import-backups/<ts>/` and is **transactional** (a mid-import failure rolls back fully — the Task-91 rollback discipline). Bundle paths are forward-slash so a bundle round-trips **Windows↔Mac**. Content is already home-path-sanitized + Poison_Guard'd at capture, so the bundle carries no usernames/secrets. **Docs (72.3) + the D-27 honesty fix:** README FAQ + CLI.md + npm-landing README now state the **"two scopes, two transports"** model (project follows the repo; persona follows the human via export/sync). **Deferred (72.2):** `cmk persona sync <git-url>` (auto-pull@SessionStart + auto-push@curation) — the task's own "deep-research candidate"; the auto-hook-integration + conflict-handling is a genuine design fork, so it's documented as the next step, not built on autopilot. **Two-pass review** added a transactional-rollback test and surfaced **a test-infra hazard worth its own task (→ Task 98):** the cli-scaffold stub-smoke runs every wired child with `placeholder` args against the REAL `~/.claude-memory-kit` (no `MEMORY_KIT_USER_DIR` isolation) — `cmk persona import placeholder` round-tripped the maintainer's actual persona (backed up + rewritten identical; caught + cleaned) before the `NON_STUB_CHILDREN` skip-entry landed. The skip is the per-command fix; Task 98 is the structural one (isolate the smoke env). Full suite 1430 green. _Relates D-27 (the wedge/niche), T2 (portability), design §1.1 (tiers), Task 76 (lessons promote — the per-fact cross-project path), Task 91 (rollback discipline)._
- **D-68 DECISION — test logging is ALWAYS ON: every vitest run (stress + standalone) writes a json result file; the old opt-in stdout-tee capture stays as a DEEP opt-in. SETTLED (2026-06-05, the user: "from now on all tests will have logging… logging written down to file").** Trigger: the Task 92 stress gate hit a 4/5 whose FAILING run predated logging (FAST mode discarded output), so the failing test was unidentifiable — exactly the cross-session-amnesia failure the kit fights, applied to our own gate. **Decision:** (1) `scripts/stress-test.mjs` now ALWAYS writes a per-run vitest json result to `.stress-logs/<stamp>_run-N.json` and, on failure, parses it to PRINT the failing test names; (2) `vitest.config.js` gained a `json` reporter (`outputFile` at `test.outputFile.json` so the CLI per-run override wins) → standalone `npm test`/`test:file` always log to `.test-logs/last-run.json`; (3) both dirs gitignored. **Why this doesn't re-introduce the old problem:** the previous capture mode was OPT-IN precisely because it tee'd stdout through `bash`, forcing vitest non-TTY → verbose reporter → ~2x slower, which MANUFACTURED new timing flakes (PR #45 / fix-stress-os-level-tee). The json reporter is a **side channel** — it writes a result file without changing console output, TTY detection, or test timing — so it's safe always-on. `CMK_STRESS_LOG=1` survives as the DEEP opt-in that additionally tees full stdout (for hard crashes / prerun failures the json can't capture). Verified end-to-end: 5 per-run json files land per stress run; standalone runs land the config file; the CLI `--outputFile.json` override beats the config default. Stress 5/5 under the new regime. _Relates the stress-gate rule (CLAUDE.md "Workflow"), D-55 (the kit's whole reason: don't lose state)._
- **D-67 FIX — Task 92 (G6) shipped: LOW-trust auto-extract drops now leave a recoverable trace in extract.log; the diagnostic log is gitignored to keep the raw excerpt out of git. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-92-low-trust-trace).** Auto-extract LOW (and assistant-demoted-to-`discarded`) candidates were dropped with no content record — only a `nothing_durable` COUNT — so a fact Haiku mis-graded LOW vanished with no auditable trace (the §6.5 "don't lose without trace" principle had a hole at the capture edge: MEDIUM got a review queue, LOW got nothing). Fix: the routing-loop else branch ([auto-extract.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/auto-extract.mjs)) writes one `low_trust_discarded` NDJSON entry per drop (excerpt capped 200 chars + reason + trust + `demoted_from` + origin), Door 4. **Log-only by decision** — NOT routed to the review queue (would flood it with low-signal noise; MEDIUM→review stays the "needs human" path). Fires inside the loop so it lands in both the all-low `skipped` branch and the mixed `extracted` branch. **The load-bearing finding (security composition, caught in self-review):** the new entry writes a RAW, un-Poison-Guarded excerpt — and the scaffolded `.gitignore.fragment` ignored `context.local/` + `.index/` + `.locks/` but NOT `context/sessions/*.extract.log`, so in a user's project the extract.log is **committed**. Today harmless (counts only); the excerpt change would make it an F1-class leak (a dropped secret reaching git). Fixed by gitignoring the extract.log (it's local diagnostic, same class as the `.locks/` logs), with a cli-install assertion locking it. **Verified vs ADR-0010** (read-before-flagging): the broader raw-`transcripts/{date}.md` committed surface is a *separately decided + accepted* tradeoff (mitigated by `<private>` stripping + Poison_Guard-at-write + documented awareness), so not re-opened here; the excerpt is a subset of that already-accepted content and the fix adds no second committed copy. **Two-pass review** confirmed (b) the else branch catches both `low` + double-demoted `discarded`, (c) `<retain>` force-promotes before routing so it's never mis-traced, (e) no over-mutation of the HIGH/MEDIUM path. Full suite 1422 green. _Relates G6, §6.5 (trace principle), Task 91.2 (the eviction-edge analog this mirrors at the capture edge), ADR-0010 (transcript posture), D-55 (lifecycle map)._
- **D-66 FIX — Task 93 (= 94.4) shipped: inject eviction is now IMPORTANCE-aware (lowest-value section first), not tail-order. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-93-importance-aware-inject).** The inject-selection half of the §19 architecture (G7 from the lifecycle map). When a tier exceeds its per-tier byte budget at SessionStart, `truncateTierToBudget` ([inject-context.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/inject-context.mjs)) used to drop whole `## ` sections **from the tail** (file order) — so which facts reached the context window depended on section ORDER, not trust/recency; a high-value fact in a late section could be dropped while a lower-value early section survived. Now it ranks sections by **aggregate value** (MAX bullet trust per section → newest `at` → later-in-file tiebreak) and drops the lowest first. The value map (`collectBulletValues`) is parsed from the **RAW** bodies before `cleanScratchpadBody` strips provenance; truncation then resolves ids on the cleaned block (bullet `(P-..)` ids survive cleaning). **The load-bearing design choice:** the later-in-file tiebreak makes this a **strict generalization** of the legacy tail-drop — when no provenance is present every section ranks equal and it drops from the end exactly as before, so **all 32 pre-existing inject tests pass unchanged** (no behavior change on the id-less path; importance-order only engages when provenance exists). **Granularity (accepted approximation):** eviction is section-granular (per §7.1.1 + the task's "whole sections by aggregate value" sanction), so a low-trust bullet bundled with a high-trust one survives over a standalone medium section — a bullet-level inversion, asymmetric with §19.2 graduation's per-bullet oldest-first. Locked as intentional by a mixed-section test; bullet-granular is the v-next stricter option. **Two-pass review:** skill-pass confirmed the strict-generalization claim, flagged the section-granularity limitation (documented in code + design §19.3) + the orphaned-valueById-entries question (inert — lookups only hit present lines, commented), and surfaced an out-of-scope **follow-up**: the total-cap fallback (Step 2 of `enforceCap`, fires only when Σ budgets > cap) still drops whole tiers from the priority tail (persona FIRST) — filed as a v-next importance-aware candidate in design §19.3. Door 4: the `tier_truncated_to_budget` event now carries `strategy: 'importance-ordered'` + `dropped_sections`. Full suite 1420 green. **Closes 94.4; Task 94 remaining: only 94.5 (live cold-open re-test, the user's outward action).** _Relates D-61/D-65 (the §19 architecture), G7 (lifecycle map), §7.1.1 (per-tier budgets), the wedge cold-open (US-2)._
- **D-65 FIX — Task 94.3 shipped: graduation now also runs PROACTIVELY at SessionEnd, not only reactively-at-write. SETTLED (2026-06-05, branch task-94.3-proactive-graduation).** The reactive relief inside `appendScratchpadBullet` only fires when a write pushes a scratchpad over cap. That misses two cross-session cases: (1) a file that drifts over its load-cap between sessions with no new write, (2) low/medium bullets that AGE past the 14-day stale window while idle. New `graduateAllScratchpads()` ([graduate-session.mjs](../../packages/cli/src/graduate-session.mjs)) sweeps all fact-bearing scratchpads (P: MEMORY.md/SOUL.md; U: USER/HABITS/LESSONS; L excluded — machine config isn't durable facts) via a new `sweepScratchpadForCapRelief()` export in scratchpad.mjs that runs the SAME relief as append (consolidate stale-drop+archive → graduate high-trust overflow), but only when over cap and writing back ONLY if content changed (over-mutation safe, no churn). **Composition (the load-bearing decision):** wired into `runSessionEndTasks` **sequentially AFTER** the concurrent `allSettled([compress, persona])` block — because autoPersona WRITES the user-tier persona scratchpads and graduation READS+rewrites them, so running it as a third concurrent task would race (the §6.8/§7.1 disjoint-input rule). After `allSettled` resolves, autoPersona's writes are complete → no window. It's local file I/O (no spawn/network), best-effort (SessionEnd exits 0 on overrun), so it doesn't threaten the 60s hook ceiling on top of the ~50s Haiku block. **Why net-positive even pre-recall (Task 75):** an over-cap persona would otherwise be SILENTLY tail-dropped by the inject layer at SessionStart (G7/Task 93); graduation is strictly better — oldest-first, archived, audited, dedup'd, recoverable + searchable. **Two-pass review:** skill-pass surfaced (a) the consolidate-inside-sweep wasn't tier-gated (only safe because the caller filters L → added a `tier !== P && tier !== U` guard for defense-in-depth), (b) the "<<1s" cost comment understated the reindex-per-graduated-bullet cost (tempered + justified vs. the accepted reactive cost). Full suite 1416 green. **Closes 94.3; Task 94 remaining: 94.4 (= Task 93 importance-aware inject) + 94.5 (live cold-open re-test).** _Relates D-61 (architecture), D-63 (94 core), Task 91 (mechanism), Task 93/G7 (inject-side selection), Task 75 (recall, v0.3)._

- **D-62 NOTE — Anthropic Managed-Agents Memory Stores + Dreams (primary source, 2026-06-04): validates D-61, two features filed to steal (Tasks 95/96), strategic positioning reaffirmed.** The user surfaced [platform.claude.com/docs/en/managed-agents/memory](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/managed-agents/memory) + [/dreams](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/managed-agents/dreams) (beta `managed-agents-2026-04-01` / `dreaming-2026-04-21`). Full capture: [research note](../research/2026-06-04-anthropic-managed-agents-memory-and-dreams.md). **Validates D-61 hard:** Anthropic's API memory = many small markdown files, **read on-demand** (only a *pointer* in the system prompt, content NOT auto-injected — *more* on-demand than us), archive-by-rename, *"structure memory as many small focused files."* That IS our load-cap + graduation + searchable-store + recall. We're **converging, not diverging.** **Two features worth stealing (FILED):** **Task 95 (v0.3) — dream-style re-curation:** Anthropic's "dream" reads a store + **raw session transcripts** → a **NEW reviewable output store** (input never modified): dups merged, contradictions replaced with latest-value, new insights surfaced. Strictly better than our in-place `weekly-curate` over derivatives — and it UNIFIES F-D (semantic dedup) + Task 66 (temporal) + Task 55 (patterns) + D-44 (curate over raw, not degraded) into one mechanism, with the D-61 no-loss invariant (review-or-discard, never destroy input). **Task 96 (v0.3+) — memory versioning + redact:** immutable versions → point-in-time recovery of ANY prior value (completes never-lose beyond tombstones) + a compliance `redact` path. **Lower-priority candidates (research note):** scoped/`read_only` shared stores (v0.4 breadth), `content_sha256` optimistic-concurrency precondition. **Strategic (the user: "this field is moving light speed fast… everyday this kit will be obsolete"):** Anthropic now ships THREE memory surfaces (Claude Code Auto Memory, the API memory tool, Managed-Agents stores+dreams). The kit can't win the *generic* memory job. Its defensible niche (D-27) is what none of these serve: **git-committed (portable, team-shareable, survives clone) + cross-project persona cold-open (the wedge) + Claude Code-native (hooks/CLAUDE.md/skills).** The play: **converge with Anthropic's architecture, double down on the git/cross-project/portable niche.** _Relates D-61 (architecture validated), D-27 (niche), D-26 (wows), F-D, Task 55/66/84, D-44; Tasks 95/96 filed._
- **D-61 DECISION (ARCHITECTURE, binding) — memory is LOAD-cap not WRITE-cap + overflow GRADUATES to the searchable store + Claude RECALLS it, across ALL tiers/files. Invariant: never lose memory; always retrievable. SETTLED (2026-06-04, the user).** The user's directive: *"we definitely need to do 'load-cap not write-cap' but memory needs to move somewhere when it overflows, and then our mechanism moves it somewhere else and Claude knows to search for it, this needs to be in all files, so we wouldn't lose memory, because the whole point of this kit is memory retention and the ability to retrieve it when needed."* **The model (= Anthropic's own, generalized to all tiers — D-60):** (1) **Load-cap, not write-cap** — writes ALWAYS succeed (files grow on disk); the cap governs only how much is INJECTED, never whether you can save. The `cap_exceeded` write-reject path is DELETED. No write-lock, ever, anywhere. (2) **Overflow graduates** — content beyond the injected window moves into the searchable fact store (Task 91's mechanism, generalized). (3) **Recall** — Claude searches for graduated memory when needed. (4) **ALL files/tiers** — MEMORY.md, USER/HABITS/LESSONS, SOUL — not just project MEMORY.md. **This supersedes D-57's "defer user-tier graduation" and extends Task 91 (project-only) to universal.** **Honest two-half split (binding on the roadmap):** the STORAGE half (load-cap + graduate-everywhere + never-reject) is deterministic + buildable now and ALONE satisfies the "never lose memory" invariant (everything stays on disk + searchable); the RETRIEVAL half ("Claude knows to search") is the ~50/50 active-recall problem (Task 75) and is v0.3 — until it lands, graduated memory is on-disk-searchable but not always auto-recalled. Pairs with G7/Task 93 (importance-aware inject → keep the BEST in the window, graduate the long tail → minimizes the recall dependency). **LANE DECISION (the user lost/overwhelmed, asked for a recommendation; accepted direction): do NOT cut a hollow v0.2.0 the maintainer won't use.** The user 2026-06-04: *"this is not a good product right now for my or my friends use… I will continue to do all the tasks until we have everything this kit promises."* So: **build this architecture next (bounded — extends working Task 91), then the v0.3 recall lane (75/84/80c); tag v0.2.0 when the architecture lands as a real milestone (no write-lock anywhere, zero loss), but the FRIEND-HANDOFF bar is the recall-lane finish, not the tag.** The path to friend-ready is FINITE: ~1 architecture task + ~3-4 recall tasks. **Process: design-section in `design.md` first (preserve the old write-cap design beside it per decision-trail), reviewed, THEN TDD build.** _Relates D-60 (cap research + spectrum), D-57 (superseded: user-tier graduation no longer deferred), Task 91 (mechanism to generalize), Task 75 (recall, v0.3), Task 93/G7 (importance-aware inject), D-24/D-25 (the friend bar reframed: friend-ready = post-recall-lane, not v0.2.0)._

- **D-57 DECISION — v0.2.0 scope LOCKED: fix the write-lock with a minimal graduation safety valve, ship, move on. In-project heavy-session recall is explicitly v0.3. SETTLED (2026-06-04, the user: "lets just fix v0.2.0 enough, ship it, and move forward, my friend can wait for v0.3.0 or even later").** Resolves the graduation-vs-recall coupling surfaced this session. **The coupling (so it's not re-derived):** MEMORY.md is byte-capped because it's *injected whole* into context (finite budget ≈ 12 facts / P-tier 4300B). So the moment a user works hard enough to exceed the inject window — an hour or two of intense Claude Code — the overflow MUST be found by search/recall, wherever it lives. Graduation moves *where* the overflow sits; it does not remove the need to recall it. Reliable active recall is the ~50/50 behavioral problem (Task 75), and **in-project recall ("what did we decide & why") is already v0.3.0's designated wow** (D-26 #2). **DECISION (Option A):** v0.2.0 ships the wedge (cross-project cold-open = USER/HABITS/LESSONS, which never graduates → unaffected) + **graduation purely as a write-lock safety valve** (search-only, project MEMORY.md only, fires only at cap pressure — Task 91). Built [`specs/memory-lifecycle-map.md`](../../specs/memory-lifecycle-map.md) (Zone-1 Spine support) by reading the code at **15 lifecycle edges** (capture→route, explicit capture, MEMORY.md append/consolidate/graduation/supersede, fact store, index, inject, the sessions pipeline, queues, tombstone, user tier), pinning design intent against code reality per edge. **10 gaps catalogued (G1-G10):** G1-G3 already filed under Task 91; the authors already knew + compensated — check-the-code again). **G6 — LOW-trust drops leave no trace** (discarded with only a count, not the content; §6.5 trace-principle applied to the capture edge) → **Task 92** (log excerpt to extract.log; v0.2.x). **G7 — inject drop is tail-order, not importance** (`truncateTierToBudget` drops whole `## ` sections from the file tail, so what reaches the window depends on section ORDER not trust/recency; can drop a high-value late section while keeping a low-value early one) → **Task 93** (value-ordered eviction, never drop high-trust before low-trust; v0.2.x). **The map's payoff (and why it's Spine, not history):** its "how to use" rule — before adding a lifecycle invariant, check the rows it COMPOSES with — is exactly the composition-verification discipline; graduation (Task 91, edge #5) composes with consolidate/append-dedup/fact-store/index, and the map names those edges so the build respects them. **Sound half (not all red):** explicit `forget` tombstones correctly (the contrast that flags consolidate()'s hard-delete), transcripts are a verbatim never-pruned backstop (nothing truly unrecoverable), fact-file dedup+reindex-on-write is consistent, inject/session caps compose. _Relates D-54 (G1/graduation), Task 91/92/93, F-D, Task 80/84, D-38 (the index-consistency class G9 belongs to). - **D-54 ISSUE+DECISION — MEMORY.md "graduation" (the 3rd shrink mechanism) is NOT implemented → the hot index write-locks; this is a v0.2.0 BLOCKER (Decision A). Filed as Task 91. SETTLED (2026-06-04, cut-gate run, code-verified).** Surfaced while investigating the cut-gate double-capture (.venv + architecture each exist BOTH as a `cmk remember` fact file AND an auto-extract MEMORY.md bullet). The design intent — stated in THREE places ([design.md §987](../../specs/design.md), [2026-06-01 lifecycle research](../research/2026-06-01-memory-lifecycle-and-competitive-position.md) lines 56+60, chatgpt-design.md) — is that **MEMORY.md is a small HOT INDEX kept bounded by THREE mechanisms: (1) byte cap, (2) stale-drop >14d, (3) GRADUATION — durable facts move OUT into granular `context/memory/*.md` fact files (the permanent brain).** **Code reality (verified, not inferred):** the kit ships (1) + (2) only. `scratchpad.mjs::consolidate()` does stale-drop (low/medium bullets >14d, hard-deleted) — `grep graduat` returns ZERO source hits; `daily-distill` touches only the sessions pipeline (`today-*.md→recent.md`), never MEMORY.md→fact-files. **Graduation, the drain, is unbuilt.** **Consequence (quantified from the live run):** cut-gate `context/MEMORY.md` = **2059 bytes after ONE session** (cap 2500, consolidation trigger 2375), all **6 bullets `trust: high`** → `consolidate()` is forbidden from dropping high-trust (line 227 `if (prov.trust==='high') continue`) → frees nothing → ~1 more session pushes past cap → next high-trust write returns `CAP_EXCEEDED` (no silent truncation) → **the kit silently stops remembering.** For a kit whose identity is "fixes per-session amnesia," project memory that write-locks after ~2 sessions is a core-promise failure. **This is the single root cause beneath BOTH cut-gate findings:** the double-capture (graduation would move the bullet INTO a fact file and dedup against the existing one) AND the cap-lock (graduation is the missing exit for high-trust facts). **Secondary gap noted (same investigation):** `consolidate()` HARD-DELETES low/medium stale bullets with no tombstone — inconsistent with `cmk forget`'s tombstone-don't-delete principle (§6.5); graduation/eviction should archive, not vanish. **DECISION A (the user, 2026-06-04):** BLOCKER — build graduation before the `v0.2.0` tag; NO stopgap (raising the cap is the band-aid the user rejected before; "is a stop gap, not a fix"). The wedge (cross-project cold-open) ships on the SEPARATE user-tier promotion path and works, but the project tier cannot ship with a 2-session write-lock. **Filed as Task 91** (v0.2.0 BLOCKERS section). **Meta-lesson (check-the-code, fired again):** I first wrote that consolidation "drops bullets to stay under cap" with "no way to know real vs duplicate" — WRONG; reading `consolidate()` showed it's selective (high-trust + <14d are never dropped). The user's instinct ("doesn't it move memory out?") was right — graduation IS the designed behavior; they only had the destination wrong (fact files, not `memory-<date>.md`; dated files are the episodic session diary, a separate track). _Relates D-53 (cut-gate run), the duplicate finding; design §7.1/§987, §6.5; F-D (fact-layer auto-supersede shares the machinery)._

Task 69 then made the **skill** the capture delivery path, and the **skill-invocation** is a SEPARATE Claude Code permission surface the bash rule never covered → the friction Task 79 killed returned. **I initially called it "not a blocker" — that was the exact lazy-framing the CLAUDE.md rule forbids; the user caught it.** **Fix (Task 90):** `cmk install` (`settings-hooks.mjs` `writeKitHooks`) now allow-lists **both** `Bash(cmk:*)` AND **`Skill(memory-write)`** in `permissions.allow` — the `Skill(<name>)` rule is the documented form ([code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/permissions): `Skill(commit)` / `Skill(review-pr *)`), verified primary-source. Fixed `seedRecentMd` to seed mtime against the same fixed instant (deterministic forever). **Meta-lessons:** (1) the multi-sided lazy-framing rule fired — "not a blocker" was the dismissal, the user was the merger pushing back; (2) the **composition rule** (check the cross-surface invariant): a fix to permission-friction must compose with HOW capture is delivered — when Task 69 changed the delivery (bash→skill), the Task-79 invariant needed re-checking and didn't get it; (3) **the manual cut-gate live run earned its keep** — this is a real friend-handoff regression that NO automated test caught (the harness exercises the AUTO path + direct cmk, never the model-invokes-the-skill interactive prompt). _Requirements: US-2 (the wedge feels seamless on a fresh install); relates Task 79 + Task 69; surfaced by the cut-gate run._

[`scripts/live-test.mjs`](../../scripts/live-test.mjs) is the scripted equivalent of [`docs/process/v0.2.0-self-test-guide.md`](../process/v0.2.0-self-test-guide.md): installs the **REAL packaged tarball** into an isolated global prefix (`npm install -g --prefix`, never touches the user's global cmk), then drives `claude -p` through the whole flow asserting **files AND tool-use at every stage** — install + `cmk doctor` 0-fail + reads every scaffolded file (safe skill, slim CLAUDE.md, hooks+allowlist, no leak); SESSION-1 staged build where the agent ACTUALLY builds + per-stage artifact checks; explicit `cmk` probes (terse/rich/Poison_Guard-reject+no-write/home-path-sanitize); skill-path safety via **tool-use inspection** (no hand-edit of memory, no leak, audited); SESSION-2 recall (tool-use proves memory vs code-read); SESSION-3 cold-open (reads built files). **Two findings the automation surfaced (the value of repeatable runs):** (a) **`--permission-mode acceptEdits` is NOT honored when `claude -p` is driven through node `spawnSync({shell:true})` on Windows** — writes fall back to interactive approval → silently denied → the agent "describes" builds instead of doing them (early runs showed "scaffold-only, no source"). **`--dangerously-skip-permissions` IS honored** (safe in the isolated sandbox). Verified via a focused probe, not a guess. (b) **In-project recall is ~50/50** — one run answered "what are my rules" from the injected persona with 0 tool calls, the next globbed the code — **the known Task-75 / D-35 active-recall gap reproduced** (passive injection isn't a reliable trigger; reading code for IN-code facts is fine per D-40, but re-deriving NOT-in-code preferences from code is the miss). So D1/D2 recall are classified as **non-gating PROBES** (reported, not failing the suite — the gate is the shipped deterministic capabilities; the gap is tracked as Task 75, deferred to v0.3). The **cold-open wedge passed every run.** Findings are a **timestamped per-run trail** at [`docs/journey/live-test-runs/`](live-test-runs/) (a subdir the doc-registry validator scans non-recursively, so per-run files need no registration) so run-to-run drift (like the recall variance) is visible across runs. On-demand, real tokens, NOT in `npm test`. _Relates D-45 (Task 89 feasibility), D-35/D-40 (recall), Task 69 (verified end-to-end on the real artifact)._
